O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine, along with its fulfillment, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to all, so the science is lost and concealed, and nothing remains of it except the little descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have made.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed, and the science is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the organization of this treatise, according to the way of exposition and declaration and of abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of the irons of cauterization, and of the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and of preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who undertakes to master the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and the conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of them, and the movement and rest of the veins, both moving and resting, and from their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates said that the name is not much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and we put our hands on the art
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, should be careful so that he does not fall into error and that he does not harm men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	so that I have seen many of those who undertake this science and if they abandon their own science and their own experiments.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut into the abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries near the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he removed with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen it called for by the traitor, and seen the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if one touches it he dies.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another doctor who took in care the duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break an open wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctors complained of ignorance holding the break on the wound by strong binding, and did not let the wound breathe at all, and they left it thus for a term;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he ordered that it not be untied;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remained thus until the leg became entirely swollen and the foot, and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had it untied, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all along the corrupted area was confirmed on the member, and not the part to heal;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and did not stop the corruption from spreading through the member until the member became completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And we see another case where the abscess bursts the swollen apostume, and then becomes inflamed due to the malignancy of its symptom.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a tumor, when it is full of melancholic humor, does not require anything but to be touched with iron if it is in the right place where one can then remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this, dear sons, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, a place where there is danger in many dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For which reason it is necessary that you take care of yourselves, so that foolish people cannot speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take your arms in consistency, and undertake your ills lightly and firmly, and make use of the better way so that by the grace of God you come to health and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let go of the diseases that bring grief and bad health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and put away from you that which makes you doubt, and have faith in you so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says distant from some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take in hand a bad illness, lest you be called foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about cauterizations of fire and also about cauterizations of sharp medicine, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of burnings, and of the cauterizations by fire, and of all that which is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of ulcers and of wounds, and of the extractions of arrows, and of similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and this chapter is ordered and are the forms of the burnings.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring the dislocations and the distortions, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered concerning the high joints of the feet, and the forms of the burnings.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Although we remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of the aid, and of the harm, are the longest speech and subtle science and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this speaking many of the wise men agree;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and my breath is scarce for their words, for I dread the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, a hot and moist complexion, and a dry and moist complexion.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion with mixed matter, they disagreed among themselves and said that cautery is of great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not suitable for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness with heat, nor with dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and it is said by those who say the opposite that cautery provides great aid to hot and dry illnesses that occur in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of man and its moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true many times through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And let no one interfere with it except he who has experienced it, and who knows through long practice the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the space of the tension;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no fear, similarly in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the members assemble and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cauterization is one of the secrets of the cures, and of greater goodness than cauterization of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not come except to the member which is burned, and does not harm another member unless by name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from one member to another by touching, and bring to the sick member the diseases of grievous sanitation;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance kills the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire through its height and through the goodness of its substance does not do this, if it is not in excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse the length of the speech, for it does not please me that I reveal to you the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should agree on what time the cauterizations should be done, and choose taking pains.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harmful effects which supervene are easily cured by the aid of the cauterization;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and meanwhile the cauterizations are for necessary pains and hastenings that cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think ever, dear son, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is healed by cauterization has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and they tell it to him;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they believe, because cauterizations are not a medicine which alters the temperament, and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for the hastening of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and of its operation.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes from the complex condition of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered in him the excesses by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if not cauterized with fire where there is little excess and moisture, as for cauterizing dense areas for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but that happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterizing is worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterizing is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for a disease and they do not work, then we administer cauterizing, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	It then appears clearly that cauterizations are the last resort of medicine, not in accordance with the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauterizations with instruments of gold are less damaging than those of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of the gold and the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the application of cauterization does not cause putridity, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauterizations of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they praised them.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And however when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know how hot it is by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	it becomes discolored from the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus it has enough impediment
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cauterization that we have shown to be suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have organized this chapter from head to foot, because it makes the journey easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	for cauterizing the olive tree
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauterizations are good for moisture and for cold on the head, and they are done because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that flow from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and due to a multitude of songs and pain in the teeth and throat pain, and similarly for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cauterization is such that the patient should be purged with a medicine that cleanses the head, three or four times, according to what the strength and the age and the habit of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient rest their head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make them sit with their arms crossed between your hands, and put their hands under their armpits;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and take your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from inside then heat the cautery that is called "olivare", whose form is this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put it on the marked place from inside, and make it descend and constrict your hand little by little turning;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and look at the place if you see the bone a little swollen;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, restart the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little wax, and put it in warm cotton inside, and put on the place, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After a dead body has been placed in a grave;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it stay there until the cold has removed the stiffness;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the wound of the joint that is called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the old ones said, that the more one keeps the wound covered, the more it purges;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason it is helped by movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should cauterize so much that part of the bone is burned, and then scrape off what is burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should cauterize so much on the bone, and strike it so forcibly that one removes from the bone as wide a piece as the buckle that women put on their belts, because the humors issue freely outside;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must let the wound remain covered for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that, one must cure and cauterize.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two kinds of cauterizations do not seem to me to be good in every way, except for certain men in whom there is a vein of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it to the surgeon;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by continuous discharges of a natural kind, as we demonstrate in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and myself, when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems more healthy and beneficial to me, and for that reason I observe in the end a healthy outcome.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the pain in the old head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in the whole head there comes chronic pain, and it lasts for a long time, then the patient should use roots and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if they do the cauterization that we mentioned earlier, it is not worthwhile.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the sick person's arm is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize the one who has been burnt a little, as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards do cauterization on each horn of the head just to the bone, as we have said before, and do the cauterization on the place that is called "vasels".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one puts a poultice.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and put your hand so that you do not feel all the way to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patients feel much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of them elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head there comes sudden pain, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged with medicines that cleanse, and one has done the other treatments that I have spoken of in the division of illnesses, and all this does not profit at all:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then one must make cauteries according to two methods, that is to say with hot medication and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauteries of hot medication are that you take a handful of herbs, and remove the bark and take a little of the head, and then apply it to the temple where the pain is held in such a manner that you can place the handful of herbs under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it has been applied, bind it and constrain it well and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie and treat with the doctrine of oil, and leave the wound thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a plaster cast in butter until it can be recognized as bone.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of unction as long as it is healthy;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that I have written about certain burning medications or the treatment of burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery made from iron, for that is its form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or it has little curvature, and in the middle it has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the iron a little gently, until the half of the spear head is burnt;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and raise your hand so that the artery does not become hardened, which is defective, and remove excess blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards put cotton in a warm water bath, and apply it to the limb for three hours;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put moistened cotton in a poultice, and then treat the limb with ointment until it is healthy;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare", to the very tip, and beware of touching the artery in this migration which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the migration
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migration as we have previously said in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous statements of medicine and iron do not suffice, then it is necessary to heat the cautery that is called "cultellare" until it becomes white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and show thus on the painful limb a line of half a thumb's length, and lift your hand once, and hold tight that you do not touch the artery and that you do not come close to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jaw that moves when one chews, and the nerves have no regard for what moves and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the evacuation of blood from the artery when it is touched, where touching it has great fear and shame for the one who does not know it, and who is not a studied and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work in the middle of the way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is touched, and I will show you where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have spoken of in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two edges;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and it is a better cautery than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears caused by cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one has applied medicines that dissolve and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing all around the sick ear, or around the two where the pain is held in both, and a little below the root of the ear since you have marked the place of the injection;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure, leave the limb alone as long as it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is not fiercer than those which move with phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of the illness;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauterization on similarities that come from bloody flux and from spitting of kidneys.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this type of torture that moves with phlegm of kidneys and purging of head and gargling, and it is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little further back from the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cauterization in the part that opens cleanly, and have it cauterized directly on the head of the ear a little below the crown of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery stay on as long as the pain of the heart is eased;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the cutellaire that we have mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary that the knife be a bit thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure of the limb as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the case of apoplexy is old and you treat it thus as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the member called "vassel" as we have said before, and the fourth cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness it is necessary to give the patient great and powerful pills that purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	afterwards anoint the head of the patient all over, and apply to the back of the head a plaster of mustard which is written or treated in the book of plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of the cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is thus healthy; it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then have three cauterizations made on the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be a space of one finger between each cauterization;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and cure him like the others, and if you see him often, and the patient is suffering, then have one cauterization made in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and his profession is, one on the two horns, and the cure as long as he is healthy;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterer be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be anointed with herbs and with that which we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterwards anoint the head of the patient, then make a cauterization in the head and on each horn, and on the back and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you are in a similar profession, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is strong, then make four cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the most painful spot is scarred, and raise your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment until he is healthy, and it is the cautery that is called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics must not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to modify the treatment with herbs and other cures that we have mentioned in the section when the patients are great and suffering from a lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot yet suffer, have them gargle and chew modifying the brain often with good meat broths;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king has made a thousand, and have it cauterized according to what we said before, and cauterize on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffering, have them cauterized as I said to the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let it be cauterized with olivier according to the method that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a woman, then make for her a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or the corrupt humors and gross phlegm are, then the cautery of hot irons as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give to drink a thing by which the brain may be purified, according to what it is stated in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After that, examine the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after make a bandage well done, like a circle, and put it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be cross-wise, and held firmly on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after apply the plaster, and take care to cover with old barberry butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and let it warm at moderate fire, so that one can boil the pus to make it suffer;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after having seen the circle from within in the head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient each week once with another good governance, until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see that it is necessary to cauterize, make many points on the entire cauterized area.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This type of cauterization resembles a brain in equilibrium;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on it cotton moistened in butter and in fat of goose.
de l’awe des eulz	from the pain of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When pain comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then give and let the patient drink something warming the head, and the guard against all humidity, and make them sweat with baths many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After instructing him to shave his head, and having cauterized in the middle of the head, and having made two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of the brain is with the two eyes together, or where one descent is in one eye;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and let the cautery reach all the veins and arteries that are close to the brain, and let the cautery be as long as the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of the discharge of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop immediately with a cloth.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and in the cutting of the cautery how you will stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery is made or a splint put behind the two bones;
dou cors des larmes	tears of the eyes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head before;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from cold and phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cauterization that I spoke of at the beginning of the treatment on the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations or branding irons under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is more swollen, then cauterize gently above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	a flux of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give the patient three drinks of warm potions;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head, and make a cauterization in the middle with an olive-tree cauterizer;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations with the cauterizer called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not touch it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery that is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	because of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that there are two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let go of it with your hand unless until the third part of the parchment is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted into a membrane, and prick the eye, and one makes cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It is to know of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cauterization, instruct the patient that they should let the hairs grow as long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in your care;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards mark on the skin of the eyes a figure that should be as wide as the width of the middle finger, and let the beginnings of the sign be among the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton in a glass of oil and anoint the eyelid with the juice of periwinkle on the eye, then heat the cauterization instrument to the form that it is:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have marked little by little several times, so that the vessels are burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the skin drawn back, and the hairs raised to the point of the nail;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three hours, then put moist cotton in a poultice as long as the numbness is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of dislocation until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And after the skin becomes calloused, and the hairs grow, then the skin is softened, afterwards recommence the cauterization on the same spot, as you did previously;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are defective, then cauterize until the skin is elevated to its natural state, and is even, and does not press on the hairs of the nail.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The medical cauterizations with burning are that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible, then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and living ashes, of each one a half ounce, and mix them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and apply it quickly, so that it does not get cold, then spread it on the shape you have made like the leaf of a myrtle, and put some on the papier of the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness holds in one eye or the other, one should open it, and if in both then also;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put two cotton threads moistened with oil of rue into the opening;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the patient be in your hand and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the hole and rub the mouth every time the patient feels a biting sensation from the medicine, for it feels like a biting as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have held it in place for a long time, then remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the morification will be passed, if the limb is lifted from the water, and examine it if you see the skin lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply again the medicine on the limb or where the medicine did not work, until your operations are even, and your eyes are set to the point;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on cotton moistened in broth until the bitter heart is cooled, after cure the limb of the joint which is called "diafonis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you take care well of your work with great care so that it does not happen that the point of the medicine reaches the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the oil, then reapply the medicine on that limb which is softened by the skin properly, thus as you have done before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment until he is healthy;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and it is the shape of the abscess of the dead flesh:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And it is known that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this will be their constrictions;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be hidden from him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not profit, then it is necessary that you make a cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does it bend its neck;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	afterwards put moist cotton on the vein or in the juice of melilot on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After heating the cautery which is applied:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped to the head like the form of a wing of a shoulder, together with which is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one side of the head to the other, and if you see, it should be also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this is what is shaped for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula, it is covered, and in drawing out the pus, and the dryness;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and it is closed, thus the work, and draw out the fluid from the belly;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after putting on the cautery hot ferment, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the kidney near the navel, so that your hands do not cause harm;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the navel, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery near the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then restart the cautery once more, and also if you are a professional at it, and let it be for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I apply a moist cotton cloth to the area, and treat the joint with a dissolving ointment until it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is not healthy, then apply a caustic medicine as long as the bone is covered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and let it be governed according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a type of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Cut into the fistula, and make the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After put in the incision a thin iron instrument of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make an amount of a kind of poultice;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold the hand or wrist firmly, and do not move the patient's joint, so that the applied poultices do not go to their eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye a moist cotton in a basin of warm water or in a bath:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the poultice if applied near the place of the fistula, and the sound part by miraculous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a probe to the navel, and to bring the fistula to the body of the navel according to what is proper for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks on the lips that are called "poil", and similarly on the lips of infants.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks of the bone that we have spoken of in divisions, and the treatment is not beneficial, then heat up a small cautery iron according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it hastily into those cracks until it comes to a flow;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, anoint the limb with cerote until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after putrefaction and decay and it becomes swollen and develops into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you apply the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron comes to the flow of it, and cauterize the area;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is thus cured, it's good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then you should uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that does not work, then put the head of the patient in your healthy;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cauterization tool whose shape will be described later, in such a way that you put a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cauterization tool between the teeth hastily, and hold it as long as your hand can, so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand and restarting the cauterization according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after the patient has filled his mouth with salty water, and holds it for an hour and spits out frequently.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in the same way the teeth that were loose are confirmed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the rotten moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or decay, and medical treatments are of no value, then it is necessary to perform cauterization in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cauterization with borings and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization with borings is such that you take borings of a cow, and put the tip in an iron or steel spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after taking cotton and wrapping it around the tip of a stick, and moistening it in hot borings, and putting it on the aching tooth quickly and holding it until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And thus do often as the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton are wet in cold broth, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron so that the pus comes to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauteries together with fire are such that you grasp an iron or copper chain, and it is so large that the pus does not come to the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heating the cautery, from which the abscess will come out after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be lessened that day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good cold broth in the application of this cautery, and then pull it back;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and it is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And perform cautery on whichever part of the head you wish, and according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and it is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofula are of phlegm and cold moistures, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery applied to that place from which afterwards comes the form, and it has two openings for the humors to issue from the cautery of the other part;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and put the hot cautery on the abscess once, or it is a second task, until it comes to the source of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small then put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on cotton moistened with butter until the abscess is discharged;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure of the limbs and of tendons until it be healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the shoulder:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors prevail over the channels of the wrist, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be treated first with solvent medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after he has undergone cautery to the root of the throat, and beware that you not come near the throat, and do not kindle the heart except a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After he has undergone another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauteries be which is called "clavicle" from which we have the form in front;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the limb as we have said before until it be healthy.
de la toust	Of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and the disease of lungs are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever nor cough, and it is a chronic disease, have two cauterizations on the chest in the veins;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery in the breast between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery be that which is called "clavicle" according to the form that was mentioned before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery that is called "poins" of which the form was mentioned before in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the poins be just to thirty, or within that.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the cure of the back according to what was said before, and let the cauterizations be at three ribs according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauterizations are made lighter, because you make three of them at one time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards the patients are swollen on their back and on their sides;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after that, raise the heart which is within the diaphragm with your left hand fingers;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then apply the cauterization which has two nerves where it is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart as long as it penetrates to the side, and the figure of the cauterization comes together with four cauterizations;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason it is made with the cautery that has III nerves, because the figure of cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the thinness of a thread and it is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery, burn with a flax seed or a flake;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make the patient rest, and not move the limb by long tension as long as it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little matter that has happened, then make a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed again, and the moisture is dried and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach there come chills and a lot of moisture as it stretches to its complexion, and are multiplied the catarrh to him, and in manners of accustomed treatments he does not profit, then it is necessary that the patient be warmed on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Of this, afterwards make three cauterizations on the skin of the leg for the quantity of an egg, on all the curved cautery, and two cauterizations on the two sides as long as the figure of the cauterizations is at three angles, and have a space between one and the other so that they are not joined together when they will suppurate;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cautery be so deep that it pierces the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a cauterization of a large cauterization in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cauterization, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach at the point according to the quantity that you see of the thickness;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize all the cauterization that is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the wound that we had in front, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When to the liver comes pain of cold and of moisture and of great windiness, as long as it is made foul from its natural complexion by the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not profit him, thus it is necessary that the patient be warmed on his liver;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, against the hypochondries, where the pain of the sides or the pain of the loins comes;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and has a space between each cauterization the thickness of a finger
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauterization be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too much on all the cauterization;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be so slightly the size of the heart, and let the patient stand upright on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then let him be seated, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauterizations of the cutaneous layer, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not come to boiling, for the heart is very subtle in that place, and one should be cautious to see;
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels a very sharp pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment of the abscesses is done, it is necessary that the patient be supported under his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark with a sign the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a razor, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize the cautery as much as the area is burned, and come up to the sphincter, as much as the perineum is entirely cauterized;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of the abscesses until he is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not suitable that anyone uses this cauterization except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have been corrected many times.
