et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is subtle, then turn it at the point of the nail, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then know that the blood does not stop at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And let the blood flow for six hours, up to three times;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it with two threads of strong double silk thread, which will prevent it from coming undone before the closure of the wound, and will come to be stopped by the blood;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then remove the excess hair that is between the two lips in that same hour, and then, if you see it, if the cautery of the cautery iron has reached the bone as long as the head is removed;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and it is the mother of work, if the patient has no fever and he is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cauteries are helped in finishing the ulcers:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is of greater aid to the ulcers.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or it is necessary for the extraction of the arteries that one fills the body with old cotton and puts it on well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when one removes them, let them be cured with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until they are healthy;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without cutting the artery as long as you work, if you have to cut with a knife by cautery, or you fill the body with vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood is congealed;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you don't have a remedy at hand, then put your finger on the spot until the blood is congealed, and raise the limb from cold water as long as the blood stops, and hold it steady as is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is more moderate in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting on both sides, but the cutting be well spaced to withstand the heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the extremities are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be between the two incisions one finger of space, and then when you have signed to enclose the two limbs, and you put the iron burning on until it comes near the bone, and cut the vein in two limbs;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and should be loosened between the two parts for it is not suitable to be tightened by this cautery everywhere.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and it is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are on the outer skin of the head, and no medical treatment is beneficial, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel the forehead with numbness as if from frost;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and the eyes are tender and moist so that the hair of the papers is burned, and the papers are scorched, and charred by the heat of the tears, thus there is need for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "bruised cure", and it is that you make on the patient who has this illness the hairs that he has on the forehead, then make three equal cuts on the forehead according to its length;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the cuts be as if two fingers in the middle of the forehead going downwards to the nose, and the other two on either side of the head above the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on either side of the head above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and direct your hand from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers at the joint across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much of cloth for sucking the blood, then push the spitulum sharply with two parts of the body where it is in the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that is above the temple just to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two fissures to the entire surface which is on the bone, then make another cut of the middle incision just to the other second, and then extract this spitulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you push into the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellaire", and it is very well cutting on one side, and on the other side is soft, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the cauterized part cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the cauterized part touching towards the bone, and the swelling as far as it comes to the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut off the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision is continuous up to what opens from the heart, and then make another cut in the middle split up to the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract equally from the blood, and press the limb for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each split a piece of old cotton, and put on moistened cloths in wine and in oil and in vinegar, and guard that abscesses do not come;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the linen, and apply a great plaster of hot water, then the treatment of the wound with basilicon oil, and other treatments that one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Two remedies for the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When in any case one has an acute cataract with severe symptoms, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and the sight weakened, and the eyelids scorched;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and the head is deeply pained with sharp pain, and the patient is in anguish;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you should know by these accidents that those matters and that cataract does not come from many veins, and the remedy is what it is, if it is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one two fingers wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and disengage your hand from the nerves of the temples that move to the brain;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then probe between the two lips of the wound and put in a lot of cotton, and bind with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then apply warm dressings moistened with wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is inflamed, it is necessary that you rub the bone as long as the flesh begins to grow, then treat it with caustic things, which cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In a similar way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flowers of centaury, and four parts of colonchine, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to these wounds to induce flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Oats, or beasts, or stone from a mine or similar things such as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, like jasper, fava beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as sharpness and acids and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone in the ear or another kind of thing that does not belong to the ear, and does not grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill a portion of violet oil or oil of cypress, then apply it for extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and have the person sneeze from the nostrils, and stop their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool in the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and stop the ear with wax.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times fever comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out, then one must perform an extraction with subtle pincers, from which this is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out to the pincers, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then perform an extraction with a subtle hook of small doubles;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out by that, then make a thread of silver and push the head of the thread through the hole of the ear strongly, and stop up what is around the thread with wax so that the veins cannot enter with the thread;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in that manner, then take some glue and take the veins, and put some instrument which has a point for that purpose, and put a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear as well as the abscess is hot and swollen, and spasms;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the cutting is that you first let blood from the patient's head, and extract blood according to the measure of its virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or dependent flesh;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be as wide as a coin, until you reach the stone, then extract the bone according to your power, and suck hastily with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then apply the spatula with a subtle touch according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with subtle pinces and with sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case then that there is a discharge in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use a first dressing of conditioners, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them be placed on that same ear where the discharge is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it flows out by itself, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If this is not so, then take many stones according to the length of your hand and hold them lightly, and heat them a little by the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient's finger in or through his ear, and rub on this side of his feet from another part, and make friction with one foot on the foot that is by the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop rubbing foot against foot until the disease has entirely gone, and thus the health is entirely restored;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see that, then take a reed, and put one of the ends in the ear, and the other end is pressed by fire until the hottest part of the reed is burnt;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do the same with other reeds until the disease has entirely gone, as we have said in the beginning.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of a beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the section;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large size so that one can feel it, then administer the extraction of splinters;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the lightest thing to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you perform the treatment as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment is not beneficial, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there appear no worms, then treat them as subtle splinters, and if they are not visible, then take the chain of what is its form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the thinnest part in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck firmly on all the chain;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff cotton into the cavity as I have said in the previous chapter;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not come out forcibly as we have said, then administer distillations that the old ones have experienced in the treatment of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with all this equipment, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or of brass, straining through the small holes, and above, covers for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and for pressing within the distillation the instrument of brass well made for this purpose, and if you see take the rag and envelop it around the pointed end with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then put your oil or your juice, and that which you see of your medicines into the cavity, and let the cane be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then thrust your fingers inside the armpit to the bottom of the socket, and press your hand firmly so that the oil is distilled or extracted from the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and let the patient feel inside, and let the distillation be heated by the fire in the same way that it is distilled in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have a passage in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men due to blockage of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it happens that the hole is stopped up, and one sees it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes from deep within, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many conditions, and in that which one sees, it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opilation apparent, if the work has all this spatula from which is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting at the front and back all even, so that it does not harm the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the opilation is of flesh or body of the ear, if you hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is all removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is deep within the ear, take a subtle rasp lightly and heat it a little by the fire, then put it into the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you suspect an obstruction where the patient feels pain in the ear, touch gently, and be careful not to press on the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent made from the width of the perforation, and the stopper in the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this on no day when the wound is sore, or take a tent and the stopper in vinegar and rose water, and powder with burnt vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you pull out the tent and put in another moistened one made from a cerate of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is reduced;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, then dip a sponge in cold water and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that reduce the flow of blood which are described in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the pimples
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	It is a remedy that comes in pimples of the eyes when they are moist and dry, so you must stretch them with tweezers and pinces, and cut the head of a spatule from its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the limb a glassy ointment spread.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not heal by itself, then the cauterization of subtle lenticy should be done with fire, and the cauterizer after the incision is of no value;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repair, when none of these things remain at their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, then their roots are burned and do not regrow.
de la gresle	of the gum
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come in pimples of the eyes a thing that seems like gum in its form and hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "gravel", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the upper and lower eyelid.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	it is necessary to know if the swelling changes on one side and the other, and it is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	feel then the thickness of the skin, afterwards scratch off each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing a little the skin, do not grievously harm the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, then assemble it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for the organs will restore themselves at once and join together.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the swelling descends inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the skin, and stretch the swelling with pincers, and cut and press it on one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the plaster is removed by cutting, it does not cause any grief;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the stone is cut, if you raise the eyelid of the salty eye, and treat the limb of whoever urinates blood so much that the patient becomes healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is discharged in threads from the skin of the eyelids, and this happens more to children than to grown people, and causes them great pain in their eyes, and they get the discharge in the morning, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this reason they often lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are found to be moist with the discharge and the appearance that the exinach has covered the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb with your fingers and feel the excrescence between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your hands;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a piece of linen, and prepare a dressing in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the excrescence on each part, then put it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the excrescence is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture on the spatula a cutting edge of such width, and not more wide than the wound one makes on the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the flesh deep until you come to the excrescence;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases the excrescence comes from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract then a piece of cloth from the middle to the fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left as long as it is sparse;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and beware that you do not put in the gap, that you do not reach the whole spatula to the hole, that you do not blow on it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the bone does not appear at the beginning of the gap, then increase the gap slightly until it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and in water, and put on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if it is one of those men who break the seal and put on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure him as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscess comes to the wound, then cure with warm poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in the papers hairs grow joined to other than their nature, and are inflamed, thus they harm the eyes, and bring many kinds of sickness such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albumen, so that it is a cause of destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the cure is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or with cauterization assembled fire, or with sharp medicine according to what is stated in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by branding, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then take the paper of the eye with your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then I push a needle to all the thread below;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be within the margin of the skin where the hairs grow among these hairs, and pull the thread to the bottom across all the skin, and turn it to the scraper;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the skin, below the hairs joined, all the spatula coping, from the large laceration to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put below the skin a small piece of cotton and of cloth, then sign on the skin a figure of ink, such as the leaf of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevate the skin which is divided in pieces.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it happens that one must cut a large quantity of the skin according to that which the skin is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make on all the spatula along the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large wound to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be one of the natural cracks near the hairs in the thickness of a root, then cut the onion at one of the two angles of the heart, then scratch everything;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle and all thread of subtle wool, and suck the blood, and make dry the excess threads on the two eyebrows with any sticky things, if you want to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then I have no cure, then leave the stitching and the threads until three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitching of dry and constricting things, for the skin will heal by itself due to the soothing of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitching is bad (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you show the parchment of a figure which is as the liver of the martyr, as we have related, to three ounces of the mixture according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then scrape off what surpasses the small equal forces according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, take a needle or thread, and put it in the middle of the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread through the large arm, and the second thread through the small one, and join the two threads equally between them;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have made a sign, as we have related, then join the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healthy;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to a cutting, thus the dressing of wax and similar adjustments soothing;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and often it happens that the hair of the papillae are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the papillae and the thread within according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two subtle threads as long as the papillae and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly on what overcomes the papillae of the eye, and stretch the two wounds of the two parts forcibly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that is held tight will die and become black and decay, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if the wound has strong forces, then heal the skin as long as it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sucked, and if the skin is lifted, and no longer pricks the hair;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and it is the shape of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width;
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a thread of soft and fine silk;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the heads and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm of length;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the flesh another subtle thread of silk quickly, and tie the head of the two threads;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head in a warm place;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be warmed by the sun so that the work may be clarified, for this is a subtle and minor work, then take the needle and push it all the way into the root of the hair next to the skin, and make it pierce the skin sufficiently until you pull it out from above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair up to the flesh, and push into the flesh that same hair, if there is one or two or three or several;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then remove your hand so that the hairs come out entirely from the flesh into the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the flesh is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the flesh downwards with all the thread that you have ordained, until the flesh comes out from the hole and so that you see it by the sight of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you will thread the needle and the string, and close the eye and let it be for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and the flesh grows.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are small, accompany one hair with a longer one from the natural eyebrows, and let it be with the one you leave, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the decay of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "alexandrion" or decay of the eye comes into the eye, it does so in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one being natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from a cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work is that you cut the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tendons of linen, and lift them until they are healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not suitable that you use it in the treatment of things that are dried and constrained.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first one;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but it has an effect on softening things, such as figwort;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose of aqua or teasel and seeds of flax being cooked, and poultices of yew tree melted in any of the oils, and it envelops a tent, and cures this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it not become sour according to the form it had beforehand;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are not aids against this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it had beforehand.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocated, truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from a wound and a cut and a cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and the stitch in the flesh, and you make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the thread comes out at both sides of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then is the flesh sewn over the threads, and the skin is cut with a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the wound returns to what it should be, it's good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take a rasp and put it in the cut, and turn the skin, and make two cuts on either side of the skin;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the head of the two fractures of the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has no "I griesche
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then sew that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are adjusted from what follows the wound, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment for what we have said regarding softening medicines, and of tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a fracture or from a wound or from a burn, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the skin, and according to what is seen before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two lips of a wound, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare everything so that they can make the body return to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patients themselves, according to what they need in terms of work and instruments in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	due to a sudden pain in the knee
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this swelling comes to men in such a way that the knee is swollen with white stuff, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor under the knee, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and stretch it to pinches, until you cut what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patients cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula does not injure the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be such that you lightly scrape away the assembled [tissue], so that the skin regrows according to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it heals all the assembled [tissue], and sometimes forms in the oily bitter sauce, and the sweet oil rises from the bile;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the skin and the oil a layer of flax, and put on the oil wet wool in abundance of eggs;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use sweet bile and hot things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the anointing with the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the anointing is in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	one is nervous and similar to a hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to a white, frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and cuts the flesh with pincers, it cannot feel;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other symptom worsens towards the great eye, and increases little by little until it covers the entire sight and the entire light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head on a tray, then covers their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and raises the paper with one hand, then wraps the finger with small bandages, and stretches it to the opposite side;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then takes a needle, and puts in it the hair of a horse, or of a cow, or of an ox, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and doubles the point of the needle a little and sticks it in the finger, and pierces it with the entire needle, and ties the finger with a thread and stretches it to the opposite side, and scrapes all the hair from the side of the finger which holds the thread and the needle next to the skin just to the head, then cuts the remaining part at the root of the eye with all subtle spatula and small forces, and lets the natural flesh or the eye, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears excessively;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail sticks to the anvil solely, and to the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one scrapes all the spatula from the softness of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And beware that the spatula does not touch the thin tissue and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision put in the oil a little of melted lead, and made from litharge, and let it stay until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure what is needed so that it becomes healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot push in the needle, and the nails cannot enter, often this type of nail is cured with medications;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have described in the section, and if you see it covered, then open the oil of the disease, and take the spatula gently a little sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And rub the unction gently underneath, and if you see that it lessens a little and the reason presses upon, then distill from your mouth into the oily colic made of litharge and red colic, and boil the oil until the other hour;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then resume the other work according to this same operation, as long as it is all bone.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, then as with a hot abscess, treat it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healthy, then resume the work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm is hindered in the oil by great hindrance, then stop at the elbow, and cut one part and not too much, so that no harm comes from it;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in the red oil-collier which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that grows on the tonsil.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In the eyes of some men there grows a red flesh, and covers the tonsil and hangs over the palate and the uvula to the throat, and resembles a rose of baluster.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work of it is that the patient puts his head in a warm place, then opens the eyes, and takes out all that flesh with sharp instruments suitable for that purpose, and holds it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the root until the end, and beware that you do not touch the oil to the working place;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the ankle and small forces which one calls ostesebel, according to the form shown after this chapter where it is demonstrated;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is cut, then apply the oil of distilled broom or you distill red collier and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the wound cotton with vinegar of eggs, so that it is assured to be free from apostema heat;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if nothing remains, and the blood is cold and dominates, and you suspect hot apostema, then leave the oil and treat the apostema with things that appease the hot apostema;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as long as he is healthy, and thus do as many times the flesh is adjusted in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless it is necessary that you alleviate the treatment of each weak oil from the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work.
des voines des eulz	Of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are red veins that are covered on the eye, and take away its function and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary first that you examine the eye, in which it is, if it is strong, and there is no other disease besides the cataract;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then bind the eye in a similar manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then press those veins all along the shoulder according to his wisdom, and let the shoulders be subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two shoulders of equal size on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then bind the forces of those veins subtly, and suck the blood from one hour to another, until you see the veins moving again outside of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not block the eyes at the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not cut except those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the cataract.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are not able to collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some hours until the pains are eased and the abscess is assured by warm application, then begin again according to this method which is described beforehand until it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and these are the forms of the fractures:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The physician calls them "arista" fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat them with cautery and burning medicine according to what I have previously said, and it is not healed, then a hole is made in it where you cut into the abscess, there where it should be drained, and all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then you scrape away all the instrument of which it is formed;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "rough head", and it should be made from iron to the rough edge, and should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the bone of the corrupted flesh, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption has been scraped;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this sometimes, then restore the place with medicines that expel.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the places are swollen, and there is a tumor, and the body of the bowel is swollen, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not suppurate and is not an abscess, and no bad accident comes, know that he is healthy;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if this is not so, then there is another trick to bring the fistula to the womb of the kidney according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you discover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is discovered, then take the iron according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the staff be tapered up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it on the bone of the arm, and remove your hand from the shoulder a little, then turn the iron all around until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by that which comes out if he puts his hand on his kidney;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the limb with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh becomes calloused and hardened, thus one sees the matter at the kidney;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open from all sides, and there is no discharge to the kidney, nor thinning, then it is necessary that you read to the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then apply the plaster, then put warm poultices or hot irons to cause sweating, then apply to the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and apply a dressing on top of bandages and of cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths sufficiently soft, and fold each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain by means of a hard bandage above, and reestablish the veins to prevent them from being struck.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then let out the veins and keep the eye constrained by day and night, and if the limbs become swollen, it is necessary that you constrain them a lot;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then untie the bandage after the day and the night, and if you see the eye getting better, it's good;
se ce non;	If it isn't so;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you reapply the plaster and the dressings and untie the bandage and the veins until he is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of the web of the membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When there is a disruption in the membrane, then it opens, and comes forth a flow of papers like a grain of resin, and it is terrible to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you cover the membrane, the work is such that you put a needle in the root of the part below next to the skin above, then put another needle where it has the double thread of the part of the armier;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have it pierced, and let the first needle according to the condition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the thread of double wire and tie a part of the vein around, and constrict it well, then remove the needle and put on the ointment moistened in abundance;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the threads cling to the vein, then treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and often the wound is constrained by the vein, each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye has great appearance, then prick at the subtle spatula which comes from the depth of the oil, and rub the moist albuginea and descend the eye, and enter in as much as;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the pouch of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not other than a boil that assembles in the eye, resembling a descending fig, and it is not a fig.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit upright and straight, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it as much as you see the boil coming out to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then be it fixed, and let it not descend and be the light disordered, and let the patient see things as he usually does;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is a fig, and if the descending of the boil is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make it on the corner of the eye a little by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner of the eye and the cornea, as long as the boil is there;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is dislocated, if it is distilled into the oil of warm water, or of warm bath or decoction, and the bandage is applied, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the warmth of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the similarities of the warmth in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce through;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if one works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and anoint them with healthy oil and bind it very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the cloth of the oil on your left hand if their eye is on the left, or on your right hand if their eye is on the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if their eye is on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if their eye is on the right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then put the point of the instrument within the crown by the thickness of a straw in the white part of the eye at the place of the lesser artery, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand as much as it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measurement of the path of almagda be at the depth of the measurement of the space which is from the plum to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the torn web, and then put the instrument as far as the vein is, then press another path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the vein descends now, then the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a brief rest, and if the pain returns by the second path, put the staff with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not ascend, extract it gently in a circular motion with your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back into the pain a bit of gum seed, and raise from that the inner oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of a spoon the oil stupes or liniment moistened in rose oil and in abundance of use, and apply with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our condition, put on the common broth with an abundance of use.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the gum cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctive gently, and do not go too deep, but make the subtle limb, then apply the ointment, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient the comfortable bed, so that he sleeps on his back in the dark room;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let him avoid all movements, and take light foods, and not turn his head to the right or to the left, and let him be laid according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then untie him in the same dark house, and test his vision, and make him see certain things, and then put him on a diet until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you alleviate this, because the fever rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	Abscesses of the sides come, that you loosen the nail before the seventh day, and the dressing of what cures the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is appeased, if you loosen the vein and put on its place a gold leaf to cover any day, and be then in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then goes out of the house little by little, and converts into its conditions;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Iraq, who told us that in his country they made a medicine called almond milk, with which one sucks the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any of it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the similarities of the forms of almagra, because those who do not know them see.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are of urine properly:
