Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And are the head of the bones of this same subtlety, and the skin in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the kidneys
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Certain times there grow in the kidneys various fatty growths, from which there are some that seem like scorpions at the base of the feet;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if it has such or it has flesh with an entrenched black color, and if it has flesh of a swollen brown color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case then of these growths which is swollen, and not entrenched, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open its nostrils, and throw the oil on those growths, and rub them with warm.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then consider that you must sustain the subtle sharp point of a part, as long as you know that this instrument is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, then open it to all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and let it heal by itself, or apply a warm poultice, and drain the fluid as needed;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize the wound as much as possible until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is burned, then apply either vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound opens, and pus comes to the palate, know that it is infected;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if pus does not come out as needed, know that there is a dead flesh in the bone above, for which reason the instruments do not come to cut it;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then it is necessary that you put a thread of flax, not too thick, and let it be known by us, and have between each knot a space of one finger or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head in the thread to his nostril so he can smell it, and pull it through as long as it comes out through the nostril inside the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times this is taught to the child in schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the end which comes out through the nostril in one hand, and the other end which comes out through the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other while we are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you see that the knots have consumed that flesh, then pull out the threads, suck the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nostrils as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Make it burn for three days or more, as long as the ligaments consume all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on a plaster of pounded herbs for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of dry medications, use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills the oils and the medications;
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or copper, similar to a covered lamp, like a chain, and its conductors;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make a closed chain, and let the instruments be flat to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the top to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease born in the head from the nose, which is called "telul", grows and increases greatly, until it becomes visible to the sight;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason it is necessary that you cut to the beginning, and remove all dead tissue, then apply the cautery or the burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and let it be covered until it becomes large, if taken in time if it is hard, of fixed color, of little sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if not the iron instrument touches it because it is an hidden abscess, for when one cuts into it sometimes, a great evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that one can cover it all, then warn the patient and cut with fear, and treat the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and burned
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Be aware that when a flow of discharge comes from one of these cartilaginous operations, it profits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then when it happens to anyone, if one examines whether the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then one brings the two lips together for a stitch, then cures it until it is healthy;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of the wound until they heal, then bring the two lips together for a stitch, and constrain them, and powder with powder of blood of dragon, and burnt incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or other warming plaster, and let it be until it adheres by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the stitch is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	By thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	To men have between the lips an abscess hard, similar to grains of beans, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you pierce the lips, and cut into each knot, and take them with pincers and cut in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then put in the brain after the incision of the vitriol broth, until the blood is congealed;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the liver of arsenic, and treat the brain with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times a flesh grows on the gums unevenly, which the old people call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the bone or the blood flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put on the limb a vitriol broth, or other powders that are astringent and desiccative;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the flesh grows back after the incision, and often happens, if it covers a second time, and requires cauterization:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not grow back after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of excrescences to be covered.
des sordens	of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Some times they gather at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth is stinking;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and take the teeth or the scabs in your hands, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make from the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, as long as they are moist;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is in the first layer, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then proceed to the second layer and the third, until you have everything resolved;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the tooth has need of various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work requires, because the rasp that one uses to scrape the teeth have other forms than those that one uses between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay as long as you can, for one should not do it hastily;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance, thus one has no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained by the pain of the injury, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth that is ailing.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and makes them pull out the good tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and however the pain does not depart from that, as long as the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already seen it be done by these surgeons;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the ailing tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with all the spatula strongly to guard the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then put your fingers or subtle pincers at the first knock and knock, until it is well loosened, then I affirm the pincers well;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in your teeth between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part, and move it as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is perforated and fragile, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with the tongs, so that it does not break when extracting;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to be very careful in opening around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And it is good to beware that you do not break it, and leave a piece behind, and cause the patient greater pain from the root of the bad tooth than from the first one.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not make a mess like the ignorant surgeons do, who through their hastiness and hardness sometimes break the jaw, and do not consider what we have stated;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	But sometimes they come from the injection of a serious disease through the roots that remain, or from the cartilage that it breaks, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is decayed, then wash the area with wine or vinegar and soap;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if a flow of blood comes from it, which often happens, then apply to the area a mixture of vitriol broth;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that is not effective, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the scrapers, where one grinds the teeth first, should be long and pointed and thick handles, so they do not bend when you grind the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be of thick metal so that they do not bend when grinding, and should be of well-made iron, and should have teeth to hold the handle.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the socket, it is necessary that you put on the spot a moist cotton cloth, one or two hours, until the gums are softened, then you push the teeth which are called "algefri", from which the gum seems to be pulled.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and let them be made sharp like a file and that is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these instruments, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a pelican, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and large so that it does not break my tooth, and if the root jumps out by itself, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if it does not, then you aid yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one is aided by this instrument which has two handles, because of its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in the front for the purpose of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, because of its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many dental instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments which are not mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are some diseases where the ancient ones did not teach the use of an instrument because of the diversity of the ills and it breaks or cracks the flesh or other bones, or it decays, if one seeks the instruments that one needs, which I have told you, and aids with gestures, because of its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-suited to hold the bone, that it does not shatter, but can be held and supported;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb with suitable medicines for that, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, thus the bone will regain its entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with the natural body, and their form is ugly, and especially in women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is born after the other tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot soothe it or file it:
adonques lou raie;	then the root;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and is made of iron pointed at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut a little and a little with the forceps in the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a file suitable for its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like the file with which one makes the nails;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and files the tooth a little and a little with light hands gently, so that it does not move until it dries;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then one smooths the surface at the end of any roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth aches, either from percussion or from cold, and the patient cannot press on it because it hurts, and you treat them with medicines that tighten, and this is of no value;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if it is necessary to constrain it with a thread of gold, because the silver threads turn green and decay, but the gold does not move;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be moderately sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to thread the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the unhealthy teeth, if there is one or several, until you come sensibly just to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then reapply the covering just to the part where you started, and withdraw your hand subtly and sensibly, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the thread to one nail, and assemble them, and pass them between the healthy tooth, and put it so that it does not bite the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then let it be constricted as much as it can stay in place, and if it becomes undone, or the threads are broken, then constrain it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it stays in place and serves thus all its tension, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two jaws, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, freshly, just as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not interfere with it, for one who is not wise and suffers, and sometimes makes the form of a tooth from the bone of an animal, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and constricts it as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper put the ligature on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes there are ligatures that come from beneath the tongue or from the nature, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	from an accidental deep wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your hand, and lift his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the large nerve thread, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if it has hardness or swelling, and it is a sudden wound, so cut the ligament and cut from the length that which holds it;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is nearby;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, lift up the leg of the patient with rosiness and ease, or with coldness, then put near the tongue a piece of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and tie the patient's hands every night, so that they cannot get up.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then put on the leg a warm broth of vitriol;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if he is without sense, then one should cauterize with the slow cautery, which is good for that.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then heal with another healing until he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see the flesh of a color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining into phlegm, and there is moisture, then one should purge the humidity, and make a subtle spit, and deliver from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if he is without sense due to your work, then put on him a mixture of vitriol until he is restrained, then return to your work as long as you treat everything thoroughly;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from clay and from seat, and heal with other healings until he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come within the throat sores called "godath", and they are properly named the II amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of small size and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will remove it, or it would burst by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and round, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument for cutting, but first take care that the abscess is warm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his hands be in your hand, and open his mouth and press the tongue under with all the instrument, because this is the form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or of subtle iron, as are surgeon's knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the thread in the hand, and thrust it through above more than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and thrust some thing of the towels with it, then cut it with the instrument, because this is the form, that seems a violent force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all of these are curved, and one is different from the other, and are very sharp, and are made of iron or of steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then cut with the nail, because this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let there be a cut on one side, and a name on the other side;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the veins, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and vinegar, and if there is discharge of blood, gargle the patient, or cooked corks of green apples, or fumes of myrtle, and similar things, until the blood is stanched;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then anoint the cure as long as it is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes there arise in the throat other abscesses besides the two veins, so cut them thus like the two veins equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had arisen inside her throat, to be sure, the abscess of the small sense;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had well taken and closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so raised that they had put two threads through the two openings of the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I probed then so much, and stuck in one of the corners, then pulled out the thread, and with it a large portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I put another thread in the other opening of the nostril, and I opened the mouth and pressed the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after that I stuck the corner in these abscesses, and I tapped on one part, and nothing came out but a little blood;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then the mucus of the woman's throat was loosened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut into that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until they became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I burned and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	unless it stays without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and may I be separated from these parts, and not be but what God made of them after me.
de l’uve	of the egg
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the humors descend to the egg, and it is inflamed and it is long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is disordered thick and round, it is called "egg".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is purified as we have said in the division, and the purification does not benefit me, and you see that the ulcers of the abscesses are soothed, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and gathered and is not lengthy;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a reddish color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the needle into the egg, and pull it out, and cut with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two glands.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut too much, it hurts the voice, and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use the ointment that we have mentioned in the incision of the two glands, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has a fear of being burned, it is necessary that you use art in the cauterization of their fearful sensation.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts their head in your lap, and then you press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and constricts it with a living sharp rod, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and then you fill the handle of this instrument, according to its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have at the head a little tube where one puts the medicine, such as the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the pipe;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient is sitting on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down the throat, and at the bladder;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand on the medicine and press on the egg, the quantity of a half an hour, until you see it become numb and the mortifications of the medicine be alleviated;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and envelop it with some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument all around the cotton on the chain above, until the cotton adheres to the egg;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry, and apply after 4 days or 5.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, restart it, and after the cautery, clean around the egg, with cotton embedded in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be aware of cold water, and be cured of gargling as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incising, nor is it cauterization;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and artemisia and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put in a seat, and make boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well plugged with strong earth, and inside the pot there should be an instrument made in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or of lead, and let one of the ends be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise to the eye through the vein, until the eye is mortified;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the recovery often happens, until the eye is dry, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of the hot abscess, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and not to make the same heat as for the treatment of an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and put inside the top a tuft of wool, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the tuft of wool does not let the greasy vapour reach the mouth, and it is a good remedy for health together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it happens to the throat or spine or fishbone, or some other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you pull what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing clearly;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear and is thrown back into the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance the thing happens through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of Turnsol, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie to the sponge a thread, and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the stomach, it will be felt, and then pull strongly;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take the instrument of a feather in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head elevated;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of it be taken, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because then it will be more or less according to what the thing is;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the swelling goes down, or it draws the instrument equally, as long as it is drawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Certain times the blood is treated with medicine, as I have said in the section, through the treatment of remedies;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when that does not benefit me, then examine the throat of the patient in the sun, then press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, if it draws to all the small veins, or has subtle holdings that are worth that.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not worth it, take a heated iron, and insert it in the throat of the patient, then blow or draw from the iron the hot steam, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full view of the cold water, and open the mouth, and throw the throat back in swallowing, and move it with one's hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the blood vessels feel the cold, they congeal.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not coagulate as we have said, then suffocate the patient with arsentid, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the egg;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because it will discharge without spitting.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are hot coals, and it be covered with a pierced cloth, and in this perforation be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you give the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but goes to the blood vessels;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and let the blood flow now, and if it does not flow, then resume the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, and has salty and foul things in the mouth, and does not drink a drop of water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary that it be forced out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument through which the blood is drawn, is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs for entering into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it has a resemblance to a hawk's beak, and has roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see this shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory recalls here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and in cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners of which one is in its own likeness same, and from that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess one should not pierce, as long as the bowel is thin according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are thick, and do not thin according to their completion, like abscesses that are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets them be for a long time while they are purulent around, by chance the ligament and the nerve of the joint become corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is located on the main limb, and you delay the perforation until it becomes ripe, then it will not harm the main limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or when it is in the foundation, puncture it only when it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is necessary that you puncture the abscess after complete digestion, except for the one that is in the foundation, so that it does not decay within, and be putrefied, and become elongated, and produce a fistula;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time for puncturing the abscess which is ripe according to the completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the separation of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and of the redness, and the decreasing of the swelling and of the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make a seat for the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens the muscles;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be of the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and in the veins and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no place for a poultice.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that swell, according to whichever member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is of value to leave the perforation as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce through the skin before that, the body will be poisoned by its venom, and will be full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they touch the lips and the depths of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you put small bandages on small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and on large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the hair, and cauterize;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become so tender as a grape, and is numb, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such ones that are cut into three angles, and if there are such ones where one cuts as with the razor of a dead body, like abscesses of the entrails;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such ones where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce the skin plainly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscesses are large, and they collect a lot of pus, that you pierce them, so as not to drain all the pus at once, but rather drain a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then press on the abscess up to the next day, then drain whatever comes out afterwards;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, a little at a time, until all the pus has come out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the vein often bursts with the issue of the pus, which by chance kills the patient, and you are not aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	End this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is small, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a flat cut, then put on dressings of linen or cotton wool;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put on each one a dressing so that they touch one against the other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or with a poultice of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it tightly for three days;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then anoint it, and treat it with oil until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if evacuation of blood occurs in your work, then apply cold and watery water, and wet the cloth, and put it on the affected area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the hemorrhage of blood persists, then apply governance and treatment, and the powders that I mentioned earlier in this book, and if it is during the season of winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary to put on tents and moistened dressings with wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the limbs are fleshy, then it is necessary to put on moistened dressings with water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then dissolve the abscess and the pus, and treat it, as is necessary, until it is healthy;
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and see it in this chapter.
des soros	Of the sores (or ulcers)
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there are boils that come from the head, and they are manners of us that are in the thighs, just like the jousting of a kidney, and many have similarities to it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	It has fat and such things where there is moisture, just like in poules;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it has such things that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no point of doubt, then the artery does not make a contrary condition.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is such that you examine all the instrument that is called "intestine", from which the shape comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then it flows through the thigh from the loin.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, then it dries without leaving anything the skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in vinegar and in oil, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those that run who have remained behind at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then replace the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains of it;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds a nut of fat, cut it according to this form, from the length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cut your lancets, and scrape on all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing to the side where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery makes a constriction, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do for an abscess if it is pierced, and to cut and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	Cut into the pierced and moist abscess, if it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if in some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as hard as a rough, harsh and white stone, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck there, one would have made as good a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming on the head, except for those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be every hour at most dependent on the flow, so that the matter can issue.
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment if as it suits
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there occur abscesses on the neck, and dislocations of the joints, and in the corners, and sometimes they come to another part of the body, and are many, and are intertwined one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its own membrane, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant which do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves from each part and is not numb at the arms of the neck nor at the artery nor in the conduit, and is not perforated;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	If it happens that you cut with a razor, and scrape each part, and the two lips of the wound are tender as a sore, then you are in this profession, as we have said regarding abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and touch it a little and a little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and it is not the tendon nor the cutting edge, which the hands hold, and do not go too far forward, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and that does not stop the bleeding, then put on the wound burnt vitriol or some powders that staunch blood, and bind the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to putrefy.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stanched, it returns to its work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look at your hand index if there remain small scrapes, if you collect and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the vein a large wound, it is not necessary that you cut that scrape at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang loose without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the old wound with cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrape, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, so that there is no remaining surplus because of the size of the scrape.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you undertake to cut at its root, and pull firmly, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrophula that have an excess of flesh, prick where it appears to be open;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and prick it as the one mentioned before, in dependence, then I will treat with unction and similar things, so that it corrupts that which remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then the treatment with unction will begin to stick, until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	of shivering
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and it is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have shivering, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat, which is called "epiglottis", be examined;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one should not trust in that, because all the veins and the part of the sickness are so that those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaw.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to remove the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision of three or four circles, or a little cutting through, between the two rings or by the quantity of the cut of the surface, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those veins are adjacent to the section of the epiglottis so that there is no point of cartilage, and the vessels are long with it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its full length, then cuts the kernel as far as it comes to the trachea.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and let the blood vessels, if you see any thing, and then cut the surface, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the flesh of the knee, which jumps due to the leg that is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound be covered with a dressing.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it gently without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Do not give this treatment unless the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the defect is in the artery.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut through the epiglottis for that which the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason the old ones command to let the wound be covered until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or in three, and then they command to cauterize the wound and treat, until it is cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the tendons of her arm.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the doctor, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and it was clear that she had not cut a vein or a duct except for the throat, and the veins had flowed out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated her until she was healthy;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and had nothing but that the young woman was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I said that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no pain.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the colour of a jasmine, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural does not cause a stranglehold.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is in two manners, of which one is similar to a fat that grows near us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it causes fear, and it is not necessary to do anything except to make fumigations in that which is small, and to prove and examine the entire intestine:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as big as the nut of a walnut, and it does not touch any vein, then cut it, just as one cuts the nuts, and take it out completely, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and treat it as it is necessary, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of us are, of which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and then it is necessary that I speak of all the difference that is between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that hemorrhoids are hot and feverish tensions, until the bubbling has passed, and is accompanied by decay.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then relieve the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With our sort there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a husk, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and increases like a tumor, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two similarities, either grey, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of an injury, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about the abscesses of the nails is that you take the most moist place that you find on the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, as much as you know that the instrument has pierced the heart, then that it be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the entromissoire, and take heed in what sort it comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture runs short, which color it has, thus make an incision as I have said regarding other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, thus make an incision in a cross, and take it with pincers, and scratch it lightly from each part and observe the coat where it lies that you pull it out whole with the injury;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it comes back to us many times;
