et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white tissue does not let the pus exit from the mouth of the wound, then you must put a probe or the instrument with which one treats the pus of dropsy, whose shape is thus before;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge a little the wound, and know that the pus returns, and is assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the entrails
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear in many conditions, because it seems to me that moving it is worth leaving it alone;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the symptoms of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the entrails;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known by excess of bitter and sharp humor, which is spread to the bowels, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it does not find a point of pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are some grievous and fearful abscesses, and of a foul color, and sometimes come from an artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not matter that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from the swelling of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this likeness, and on the other painful places;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut around the area of the abscesses, then are the veins elevated, and pull the skin of the white surface, and deliver the swelling from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already swollen with these new wounds, then it is necessary that you pull the vein, and cut around it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is near the surface, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver the entire tendon, and cut around it equally.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the wound is in the rear vein, then it is necessary that you cut it entirely, and extract the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the work is completed, apply the wound with a dressing of warm oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the entrails
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a swelling, with the softening of the entrails, and the patient feels grievous pain when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this illness is as well prescribed anxiously as the one previously mentioned, and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a seat or a bench, then apply to him the suspension of the entrails below your fingers, to all the vessels which are near to the anus, and bind the thighs, and stretch them forcibly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with the spatula knife widely through to reveal the vessels, as long as they are discovered, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then he fixes a needle where there is a double thread, and ties it to the first joint where the vein has come, and ties it again at the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then he cuts them in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupted tissues;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then he cures the wound like the others or where a bone is exposed, so that no vessel is seen that nourishes one of the intestines;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for from this comes no harm, and if all the vessels are near, then it is necessary to cut through the intestines to all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the bones do not lose their nourishment due to the cutting of the vessels, and dry and cannot be helped;
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The coming of this flux is by the section that comes from the spleen, or the tension on the belly in the area of the shoulders, because the intestine descends from that rupture to one of the intestines;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this dislocation is from the double joint, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	from a blow, or a jump, or a fall, or from lifting of a heavy burden, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the symptoms when it is from the extension of the joint, are that they come on gradually and slowly, over a long period, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal up to the depth, because the joint presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the symptoms are when it is from the dislocation of the joint, that it brings on sudden severe pain, and there are various abscesses appearing beneath the skin, and it is because of the issue of the intestine and the body at the fault of the joint.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines slip with the intestine, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with fear, because it makes them want to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to put their intestines back in with their hand inside the wound, if it can be re-entered;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let them be supported on their neck, between your hands, and lift the hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the intestines from along the length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the liver of the waist, pieces according to that which you have need to open the wound, and let it be such that the bones can protrude;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the surface that is beneath the skin of the intestines, until the white surface appears uncovered on all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your index finger in that which guides the intestine, in that which is between the white surface that is beneath the skin of the navel, and between the second surface, and separate that which is behind the navel, and between the second surface;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move to the right hand inside the heart of the intestines, and let the white skin be above on your left hand, and lift the vein to all the skin towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister that he stretches the vein upwards, and unties what is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your fingers if there is a point on the intestine enveloped or white skin hard, and if you find anything, then push it to the bottom of the belly;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle where there is a thick thread made of many threads, and push it into the back part of the skin, which is after the skin of the intestines;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the hands that appear with threads, as long as there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the skin, which we have said is behind the skin of the intestines, with a strong ligament of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the heads of the veins, and bind them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter, lest the abscess that is there not grow.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the third vein according to the first long two fingers from that one, and after these two veins leave enough space which is hidden near the heart of the intestines the size of a finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is next to the skin of the intestines, as far as the blood and the bowel, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then anoint the moistened wool with oil, and put it on the wounds, and I will anoint the vein that we have spoken of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the said bladder is cauterized after the incision, due to doubt of excessive blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens often, and leaves the string alone until it cuts through by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it is late in healing, then apply a warm poultice, and put on that which we have said, until it cuts;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this disease I have never seen anyone who dared to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancient ones said that it is made like the disease which is next to the liver, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above and below lightly with a thread;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of that which is swollen, until the vessels dry;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes the joint comes out of its socket, as we have said, and separates the limb;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and it doesn't touch any of the intestines to the cotyledons, and if it touches them, it's a little, and repairs all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it stays too long in this spot, the wound or fistula grows, until the intestine touches;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the fistula that is at the joint, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and the limb becomes flabby and separates;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and its treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously said;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient puts his hand over his back between their hands, then cuts the limb of the dislocated joint with a large scalpel according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the abscess that is beneath the skin where it swells, then take the razor and put it on the apparent place of the abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press on the deep part of the belly, then cut the two apparent places of the abscess on the edge of the razor, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the edge of the razor, and do not touch any part of the abscess nor extend the opening to anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of the ulceration of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then cure it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it becomes inflamed and cure the wound, until it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted, and has no appearance on the outside, and the cauterizations are applied to this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times is softened the skin of the intestines in some men, because the inner layers that are inside are made soft, and it is disgusting to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is a job, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on their back, and to cut the skin that has become soft on the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together with a suture, and you see, first cut away the excess of the softened skin to three or four firm sutures;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the sutures, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the castigation
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Purging is abhorred in our law, and for this reason it pleases me that I do not speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary to force it for two manners:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the physician hastens to respond when one asks him, and in haste the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of the flesh of certain beasts to help us, such as of goat and of sheep and of cat and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by traction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we do by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the member is softened and hanging;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then we take it with our hand, as long as it is loose and you do not feel them anymore.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the cauterization of the thigh:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the thighs with your left hand, then lift the penis, and cut above each testicle, when you have them well exposed;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let none of the thick skin and the subtle skin which is on the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of punishment is worse than that which is made by traction, because in traction there remains by chance some thing of the entrails, by which the beast desires filth;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners in men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two entrails open as well as the figure of the nature of a woman, where it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the fist as a rod and two entrails.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the man and the woman is that you cut the adjacent flesh all, and heal it as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the intestines, there is no point of cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenderness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tenderness is an ulcer located on the natural part, as it is too shameful to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have had it so large as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tenderness with your hand or with tongs, and grasp it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not pull too much from the bottom, lest a flow of blood does not come, for one cure drives out another cure until it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and for another ulcer that grows at the mouth of the marrows, and fills it, and by chance breaks out, and is similar in appearance to a cow's, and for this they call it the ancient "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to amputate, as we have said the incision, and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of rheumatic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Rheumatic is that which when the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or the passage is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to her;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is from sharp adjustment, or of subtle and thin sieve, and is made deep in the marrow, or in the ribs, or in the back, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception, and childbirth, and by chance the flowers have to wither;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this thing is through the examination of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears near the thigh, or to your back or to the hip.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle and thin humor, and it approaches the lungs, then hurry, and anoint the joints:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then feel the two lungs strongly, until the subtle humor is gone, and let the stoppages be covered;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take the vein, and the mole in oil, and put it on the body, and give the woman a house remedy each hour, so that she cannot suffocate.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the humor is hard and thick, then it is necessary to cut the similar spongy tissue resembling a molar tooth.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stoppages are of flesh origin, then let it be supported on the shoulder and cut;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and apply the blood-stanching medications, such as acacia, dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed with a little oil;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then anoint a plaster of wide lung, so that the wound cannot suppurate;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it be for a long time, and anoint it with a plaster of dry flax;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let it be cured with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes a sharp humor, if you treat it according to this method, unless it is an abscess that has become enclosed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the enclosed abscess that is in the marrow, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without warning flow, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become hard.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that the hemorrhoids and the thigh, when they are deeply in the marrow, and do not appear to feeling, if it is not the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, afterwards apply the poultice as a bandage, and cut at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as aconite and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then soak her feet in a warm bath for an hour, then put her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if a flow of blood comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumach and bark of pomegranate trees and gall and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster to put on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is strained, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, then have made warm applications on the back and to the same sides to strike;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take a woolen cloth, and the extract in juice of plantain or in juice of aglentier with old wine, and apply warm to the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has burst, then treat the limb with ointment as long as it is sore;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles the rough head, if it is necessary to scrape as I have said the tumour;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the marrow, such as cancer and abscesses that burst and herpes and eczemas and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary then to describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that affect the bowel.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look at the abscesses when they begin to arrive, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make it measure until the pain is appeased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and let him have two small seats where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring his feet together with the parts separated from the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a binding bond;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the abscess towards the right side, and introduce the instrument through which one opens the mouth of the marrow, from which afterwards comes the discharge;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you go to administer this instrument, that you first determine the depth of the marrow, so that what enters into the instrument does not come more deeply than it should, and that it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instruments are too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instruments do not injure them;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he puts the horn of the instrument to the bottom, and that he holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses are open, and one makes a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover the head with a spatula or a sponge.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, then it is necessary that you put in the wound moist bandages in rose oil, or in dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tent or suture of the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and put through the marrow and on the finger a clean linen bandage in water or vinegar so that it is cooked;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat afterwards for 2 hours of applying heat, having it on until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes raise the marrow and the wound with a syringe of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristolochia being cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the heat treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound grows in the marrow, it is necessary that you protect yourself from iron cauterization, but rather treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is proper first to know the shape of the natural swelling of the womb, and these signs are when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Then the sinews of force hasten to issue forth;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	But it is known that these infantements are according to the natural figure, and they issue from their head, and the second with them;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press his belly, so that the sinews issue all at once;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends to its head, the secondine goes with it, and the marrow is cleaned of its superfluities by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes to its feet, and comes to the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes to his belly, or to the liver, and is converted by accident over his neck, and by other evil figures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	it is necessary for the healer to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes out naturally onto its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the strength of the womb is weak, then make her sit on a seat, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and let its natural oil or heated poultice be applied, and then put the bath between her two thighs the small suppository of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and cut the secondine, and apply to one nail as much as the moisture that is in its shank bone;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's stomach until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with a massage of heated poultice with oil of cypress;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her press and strain with condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	now the infant will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands become dislocated, then it is necessary that you reset them lightly little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the seat from the ground, and hold the woman, so she does not fall due to the removal;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant is dead, then cut the hands at the joint which is situated in front, and extract the infant, and reset similarly;
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the extraction of the infant from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes to its feet, then it is necessary to push from above;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to the hips, if it is ordered to grip, and the hand is made to press on the condyle;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it rises too much, then God wants it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't go too far as we have said, if it turns little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it doesn't come as we have said, take a mixture of oil and wax, and melted gum, and pound all in the mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and apply this ointment to the nature of the woman inside and outside, then make her sit in hot water until the bottom of the hips;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened from below, make her a poultice of myrrh, and put it below, and let it stay for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make her sit on a seat, then make her stretch and hold her mouth and nose, and press her stomach gently, for the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, thus I put its ball in its hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then let it be laid on its neck, and its feet hang down, and let it sleep on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands little by little, and then press its hands on the stomach, and remove the cushions from beneath, until it is prepared down below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant does not jump, then take its feet and move them gently, then move the stomach upwards, then I move its hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and rock the infant little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to grasp herself as much as the infant is coming out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the exit of the child who comes with one hand while
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to put back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be put back, then make the woman get up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then have her sit on a bed, and take off her tight leggings;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then anoint the muscle that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she is not delivering, then have her sit on a chair, then try to put back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to its natural position, and have her exert herself, and instruct her to grasp herself as much as the infant is coming out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the exit of the child on its neck, and having expanded its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back;
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the patient holds his hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts the arm lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, put on the natural muscle of the shoulder and the elbow, as we have said, then instruct that it moves little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make him sit on a seat, and instruct him to take himself in hand;
et la fai esternuer.	and make him stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for the whole second finger
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner for the whole second finger, cut the second finger to one nail, until the mucus is evacuated;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it swells on his face and on his neck, cut it from the throat, so it is not retained, and the swelling decreases;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then take the child inside, as long as you have put it as it is necessary, and instruct the woman to take herself in hand at any time:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then one must treat it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the discharge of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if they have a rare name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that it is because they are multiplied, and are divided by the blood vessel which separates them, which is tied to the navel;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally like one body, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out completely, then the treatment is as we have said, and let the subtle bath, and do and handle lightly what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do it as it is worth for health.
de plusors enfans	Of many infants
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and all are fully formed in the shape of an infant by the measurement of the wise glorious sage, and it is necessary that the wise woman knows all this, for by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	thus do according to what is necessary
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead or stillborn child, as I have said in the section, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform a manual operation;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her legs be bent downward, and her thighs be raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and let the midwife take charge of the two parts, where she should be tied to the bed so that she is not treated with the downward movement of the infant;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the newborn with a mixture of oil made from nuts and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint its hands with these oils and mixtures;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently press on the newborn's legs, then turn its body to where it bends its knees that are suitable for this, and take care that the infant is prepared so that it descends upon its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if it fixes its knees in its eyes or in its neck or in its mouth or on its palate or under the beard or in the jaw or near the ribs, and if the downward movements are upon its feet, then it fixes or pricks them with tender ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he takes the ankle in his right hand, and puts the curvature between the two fingers of the left hand, and bends all his hand lightly, and fixes the ankle in one of those places that we have mentioned, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the ankle:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix one against the other ankle, or you who are in this profession, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, for the muscles to exit, and let the ankles be held by the muscles, as this is their shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then anoint the joint with some of his fingers of oil, and bend it in that part, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains a point of it, then put this ankle or higher place, and do that until all the fluid comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to the strain, then you must wrap it with a bandage, until it becomes whole;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then put the cup on the joint of the sole or the heel, and thus you must do on the other hand, and on the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is stuck in the birth, or it has the head tangled with the shoulders, then you must push the spinal vertebrae between your two hands, and make the head and extract the shoulders;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it to the instrument that is called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus same make the veins have a large natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then draw the bones to the tendons, and if the head is thrown out and it is strained by the strength, then let it be split, until the moisture that is in the foot issues out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot exit, then cut it by pieces from the mouth that you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is stuck in the belly or between the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce through so that the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the needle is on his feet, then the attraction is light, and the dressing at the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or in the chest, then it is necessary that you extract it with a draped bandage on the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or the chest, so that the moisture that is there can flow;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other limb is swollen, and the head remains, then put the bail of his hand in the depth of the wound, and pull it just to the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts one or two fingers, and pulls strongly;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the abscess is narrowed by the hot aposteme that has come to it, then it does not matter to make an effort, but rather to apply moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and let the plasters be applied, and put on a soft, moistening and soothing poultice.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the vein is on its ribcage, and you can put it in place, then apply what we have said for a living infant;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and let no one touch it, if the skin is torn apart in pieces, and nothing will be left of the secondary.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then apply what we have said regarding hot abscesses that come in the marrow;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a discharge of blood comes, then it should be stopped with a constricting poultice, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had an infant that had been dead, then she conceived another upon that one, and the other was dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long tension, a abscess came to her womb, and swelled so much that it burst, and began to suppurate greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly had no bones to point of having bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I searched the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman urinated for a long time afterwards, and little by little issued from her body;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recorded this chapter before because of that, when a master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the hammer back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Then comes the shape of the presser, to which one gives the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and it turns to the heads of the two strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	In every way, the horns should be more subtle on the constrictor, and made from ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the staff should be one finger in width, and the margin of the trees two fingers, and a palm and a half in length;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same staff, which are attached to one and the other, a half palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the hammer to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, to its similarity more subtle and lighter, is made from wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the similarity of the tanneries.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two joints, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the woman's belly with all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, the feet hanging and the legs spread, then put the two joints joined together in the belly, and hold the head of the instrument separated between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand with the instrument, as you have done with the tanneries equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the belly, until the ball makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all mounted on top, and are multiplied in their similarities;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the eyes are prepared, it is much more swift the work, and higher for men their ability.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessities are not an excuse.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in the infant, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her expel the mucus, and hold her hands at the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she spits through that, it's good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take the vessel, and make a poultice or clyster, and put in it herbs that can open the mouth of the throat, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or put in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	Then put a cane or stick through the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the abscess, and pull tight so that the vapors come out from inside the abscess;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then do the treatment, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary bandage is too tight.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not loose, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in masticatory of nutmeg, and then anoint the nature, and remove the bandage;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, if she takes it and extends it little by little straightly, so that the abscess does not burst from the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but first move it gently to the right and to the left, and then pull it;
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and is loosened.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the thigh is tightly closed, we have said the treatment of purification, and of smoking with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that which we have said, beware that you do not falter in the treatment;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the thigh, that you bind it to the hip of the woman, then anoint her with a four-part ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the poultice and plaster are applied, and come to a fever;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, when it suppurates if bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and harasses the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	If then it is necessary to have fumigations suitable for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	some of the ancients have experienced smoking with crotons and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one treats women for retention of flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen similar to a chain, and put the thin head in the nature, and the wide feet on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the dyer as long as it is wasted, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but instead the upper part is stopped up with a thin syrup:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary for the nurse to pierce that upper part with her finger, and not to pierce the spatula of the gut, and to warn the child that it does not touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the mole a moistening of wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, then put or pass a chain of the pelvis, and let the hands be still, and be careful when the infant wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes there comes sudden swelling from a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to treat that one suddenly:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	it should be treated, as we have said concerning the chain of the pelvis.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from the anus are an annoyance, and worse than those that come from the fundament, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or several;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that annoyance is ancient, it works, and brings forth moisture white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by what comes out or excretion or flatulence when the patient has diarrhea, and by chance in jumping of the blood vessel.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that reach up to the bladder, and up to the middle of the rod;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they come through to the joint of the thigh, and to the top of the hip.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the fistula that penetrates to the bottom, and does not penetrate:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your right index finger to the bottom, and apply a subtle needle of copper or iron in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then you apply a thread of subtle flax, or a horse hair, until you feel the thread or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come through with diarrhea or flatulence or blood, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	let it be that she does not perceive anything;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is next to the bladder or next to the passage of the urine, if it affects the urine, and cannot be cured by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is perceived next to the joint of the thigh, then the tender vein comes next to the limb;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of the pain inside, then it is that it comes from the bowel, and no medicine or poultice is of value;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas next to it there is no cure except for work and vanity of foolish surgeons who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is not next to it and is not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient puts between your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then probe with a tent of scarification, or of pulse if there is torsion, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it within the foundation, then you should put your right index finger, if then you feel that the probe has penetrated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and is discovered where you feel between your fingers the skin or the flesh, then know that it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if not operated on, then one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can indeed heal some of them well with a poultice, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that is made, if it is that one cauterizes subtly according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and heat the poultice thoroughly in the fistula, until it comes from beneath the foundation;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these fatty tissues are burned, which resemble a feather of a bird;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with moist tents in butter, until that fatty tissue is softened, then treat with a greasy ointment sticking and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	Unless this is done, nothing else can heal;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it is inserted between, and does not penetrate just to the knuckle which is at the foundation, and between your knuckle and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of skin, and you see the fistula in this which shows the covering of the tumor;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and apply a poultice beforehand to the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tendon will be delivered, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then I define those empty and withered members which seem a single finger, and nothing remains of them.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes to you, and cuts between the skin and the vein, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cauterizations bring together two bone things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the joining of these withered members, and the stopping of blood and the drying of the moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat the moist tendons with butter or broken nuts, until the limbs are supple and free, and put them back in their place in the bow.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the dislocated joints with a harsh dry medicine, and these are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from deep within the foundation, and it is separated from the body, then anoint the finger with the foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between two is the web or the siphach or veins, or it is pressed to pierce, if there are not other than the way of relief and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut from the bottom of the wound, or if you can place tents and cure as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deeply, so that you do not cut the tendon which holds the foundation, and come with the evacuations according to the will of the patient;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by adventure it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound after it is cut from the bottom of the foundation, or by a tent or other sharp instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then anoint the wound with the plaster that is on the spot, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part against the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes are fistulas in this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is or touches the bottom of the foundation under the skin, if take a needle pierced at the head in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I push the thread through II, and push the needle with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it passes in the margin of the bottom within, then pull out the thread from that which has passed through, thus that you push your finger on the bottom;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and assemble the two parts together, and hold one to the other, and let it stay one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it several times, until the threads join these parts that are between the two, and stick together;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, make it penetrate in all ways that you can, if the abscess is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to make a cut for the fistula if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinous spatula that one makes for the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not on the other side, because one should not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the fundament, like a grain of resin, and some are small and others large, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they are below the fundament and at the head of the fundament;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are outside have little moisture, and often a bit of yellowish or greenish discharge, or a bit of blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them within the fundament, is that you instruct the patient to strain himself by going to the chamber, until the fundament is emptied, and the fissure is apparent;
