Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein in the left hand is useful for the disease of the spleen, and do everything just as I have told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the spleen is useful for all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the liver, and retention of fluids, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and of the old hams and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its vein is that it makes the disease go from the foot to the cold leg, and rubs on the vein as long as it hurts, and loosens above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and this vein is at the calf, and above the foot many veins go to the kidneys;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Let the wound be then or more wide, at the shins or at the ankle, where it is most needed.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat the wound on the foot, beware of the tendons that are disordered, and the sinew that passes across as in cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot issue out, put the foot in a warm water, and let the vein be well purified.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bloodletting fails the first time, recommend the second at a little distance, for the limbs are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not be afraid of touching the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the saphena vein of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the thigh, and its bloodletting is good for the pain of the hip, when it is because of hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his blood is such that the patient goes into a bath, and extracts from above the ankle four fingers in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, then let the blood flow in all the ways that you can, and by penetrating;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is of more value that you collect it, for the blood is healthy, and it is very useful to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then let blood from the one that appears at the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make the blood flow as much as you want, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and extract;
ele est maintenant sanee.	he is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	of the bleeding of the intestine
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Intestines are made of horns, or of arteries, or of veins;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is done according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by striking and extracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation which is without striking is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation which is done by striking and by extraction of blood is done in thirteen places of the body, of which one is all in the sum at the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventose under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventose of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventose on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventoses in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventoses of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the veins of the two knees;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the venesection does not draw any blood, because of the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one does not become weak, as one does from the letting of blood from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor to any hot application, in any disease which comes from excess, as long as the body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to perform a bloodletting, or due to habit, we administer it at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience excess and redness in their face, and in their head, and on the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such as spit a mouthful of blood, and have their tongue swollen, and vomit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if they are among those who dream, and see in their sleep blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and measure how it is in the middle of the month, we instruct to take a purging after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the nose helps with the pain of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that it be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this purging is in place of the saliva of the head, and it is not necessary that it be used by one who is of a cold complexion, or who has diarrhea, for this causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it is not necessary that the old people use it, nor those who have cold illnesses of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often suffers from it becomes oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to put the bandage a little further down due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The application of the bandage on the neck is in place of the sore head and of the basilic vein, and for this reason it is useful for the constriction of the chest, and for the fissure of the channel of the forearm, and for the cough, and for the repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to loosen it a little, because if it holds too tightly, it induces oblivion or vomiting of the stomach and of the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The bandages on the two sides of the neck are useful for the pains of the head, and for eye injuries and migraines, and for strangulation, and for the pain of the roots of the teeth, and are in place of the soreness of the basilic vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the bloodletter to press his hand on the spot, so he does not cut the artery, and does not show signs of evacuation of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The bad smells from the mouth are a sign of illness of the mouth, and of corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is located on the blood vessels of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bad smells from the shoulders are a sign of an illness that comes from heat and from fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The bad smells from the elbows are as much as from the three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these thick veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the bloodletter that he should not make a cut too deep, because the limb is nude of flesh, and has nearby nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The bloodletting that is on the buttocks is suitable for hemorrhoids at the fundament, and for similar illnesses, and it is necessary that the bloodletting be large, and of iron, so that it has the ability to treat well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it is subtle, it will break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The ulcers of the legs appear openly, for they attract blood from the whole body, and are worth the old pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and bring back the flesh;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of the two hips, and of the two thighs, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring about pale color in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the ulcer is that you apply it first gently, and immediately afterwards, and put it firmly, and rub evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appearing with the redness of blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then do it, and put back the ulcers, and take heed to the disposition of the body, for there are some who have such hot blood, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deeper;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtly open the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is very deep, it is necessary to strike the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to let out a little blood, it is enough to suffice only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we begin again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the wound is deep, strike deeply, and stop if it is that the blood flows suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who has narrow pores, that you apply to the limbs ointments which are penetrating and resolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is anointed with oil of violets, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of seed of gourd.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is treated with oil of cress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the discharge is thick and cold, take oil of marshmallow, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who has a tender and large pores skin, it is not suitable to apply oil, but it is suitable to wash after the application of warm rose water, or cold water, or water of mallow, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has a lot of moisture, rises with ease, or with water of myrtle, and of sumach, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or with water of sewage, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or with other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not suitable to apply a poultice of warm bath before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is not suitable to sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that he be warmed, when he must be poulticed and when he is poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And let those who are bilious be warmed, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce to the vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and avoid fats, and flesh of mutton, and damp meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine made from old and new, and a little ginger, and a little cinnamon and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the more it is windy, one should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is good to give some men a little nutmeg or musk before and after the movement of wind, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be subtle, but it is not good for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The bloodletting that is done without pain is that which is done on the vein of the arm, and on the elbow, and in the hollow of the belly, and on the navel and the buttocks and the loins and the thigh, because these members do not suffer from being pricked, and it does not cause more harm than to attract blood from member to member, as we put it on the breasts when the child is suckling;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To treat the viscosity that is in the limb, as we apply warm poultices to the stomach and to the navel to soften the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, then remove it by its attractive virtue by chance the obstruction, or evacuate the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and let it be done when one applies it to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these poultices are administered empty in order to suck up the humor;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain or with hot water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with warm water, or with water in which one has cooked herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the poultice administered to the fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and it has the cost on the inside of the middle of the small perforation, just as if to push a needle, and let it be of silk, sewn in front so that it does not harm the patient when putting on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it has in the middle a rod of silk or iron across, to put an infusion, and let them be big and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the veins of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must then put this vein on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or the plaster, and put it in the vein across the rod that is in the vein, so that the clarity be at the bottom of the vein that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and let your fingers be on the perforation that we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes in, and remove the ventilation.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the plaster as before, and recommend it often, if you have the profession.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventilation then which is administered in disease of pleurisy, to all sharp, has no point of edge nor of perforation, and is not administered unless when it is full of sharp, and is put on the member as soon as.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Salves are not administered unless on members where one cannot put dressings due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the bare flesh of the body, such as fingers or toes, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is that when you find sweet, delicate, and clean bandages that are on hand, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a sweet bag, as long as they are familiar with it, and do not have anything in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cured of the vein and the intestine, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat, and will close, if it is a joint or one can put an intestine, one puts it, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the joint from the bottom, and then from the bag, very well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the joint is too sore afterwards near the body of the bandages, then wrap it in a linen cloth in a cold bag, and put on, until the bandage is stretched;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if his blood is multiplied, then put on a poultice made with vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is dried;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the body a poultice of crushed and ground beans, and let them stay until they adhere to the body, then it will staunch now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you are not skilled in this profession, then take other bloodlettings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bloodlettings do not want to take, then rub the body with fresh blood, or you prick it with a needle until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling, then powder on a little of powdered aloe and crushed celery, or cinder, and they will dry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish men scorn this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they learned from letters;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is estranged in our land, for I have never found any good there;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know not, except that by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have shortened it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two previous chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we speak in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and stays on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsions or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to anoint the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents you, as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tension is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and let the cold humors be treated with cool remedies, and a diet of cold fish and of pork, and do not drink wine, and let the treatment be without greasy foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no suspicion of hot abscess, or of matter accumulation in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his previous government, he must use it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to mend, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that cause a large increase, or have viscosity, such as roasted game in a broth, and pork, and thighs, and feet, and stomach of a calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a warm nourishment will repair the damage and be more beneficial for the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot be well mended or reunited according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but to heal, reset the bone and the large tendons that are separated and joined the limb together, so that it becomes strong as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not at all from his work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish him with thick foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the joint, and another while bending, as when the cutting of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with a wound, and a fracture is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own engine, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory recalls in his body;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by what the joint is twisted, and apparent well by swelling, and sensitive to the pressing of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no point of fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but he can still have a twist, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move the limb, but apply medicines that come next, and then constrain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that occurs in a joint, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them in place equally, just as abscesses of the feet come to life;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if a hot abscess comes, then let it be until it is soothed, as long as the abscess remains hot;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it in place with the limb that you can lift easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of this or that where there are fragments;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then hold tight, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone in the foot is fractured, hold it with two parts, whether it's the hand or the foot, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are disjointed, reset by all means the additions in their places in the members as you can, and beware that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to their true forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if the dressing is done properly, and it is not held too tightly, nor pressed as those do who make their work come from a warm abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well that they should not move it, neither while awake nor while asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secured that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is in place, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of a broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are different in size and in length and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to envelop them with a bandage of soft and subtle linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are thick, like the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the entire limb, and constrain equally from all sides, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then put light splints inside, three or four according to the limb, and constrain the hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and constrain less, than the fracture then loosen a little the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little at a time, until you press a large part of the limb into place, then take another bandage, and turn it around again above the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and constrain moderately, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first treatment above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the swollen limbs padding of linen or cloths, as long as it is all even, then tie everything with a bandage above, and then put your instruments in place, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, then apply something that appeases the abscess with heat, and which removes the inflammation, and leaves it thus for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then extract with your instruments, and let it be of a mixture of a large chain reckoned wisely, or of wood from which one makes the splints, or of roots of palm, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the instrument which one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold steady on the staves as you did in the first layer, then put a thread of cotton underneath, just like in the first layer on the bruise.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The tighter it is underneath, the less there is;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and made of flax or linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of foolish people who make their ligatures with twisted flax cords, it is a great error, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that it have between each stave less than two fingers of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is distressed by the sides of the staves after tightening on their healthy skin, then put beneath them a piece of flax or a linen plaster, so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the chest is broken, I will tell you about the treatment that follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to stretch these tendons on the first day when the limbs are broken.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put these tendons under tension until after 5 days or 7, or more according to the severity of the abscess and the heat that supervenes;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and you will see the method of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take the flour that one holds at Paris from the mill, and mix it with plenty of water, and put this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster for restoring fractures in many situations, and likewise for women and for small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster for restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the sprain:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take barberry and lady's mantle and pennyroyal and aloe and Arabic gum and moguet, a pound of each;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, five pounds;
alechil VIIII З.;	of electampra eight pounds;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make into powder, and mix with oil of wolf's bane;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the temperament of the man is cold, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores the broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is good for a sprain:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take moguet and filipendula, a pound;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, eight pounds;
acaice VI З.;	of acacia six pounds;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Take the bolica armenic, and boil it well, and cook with water or oil of buffalo, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat the joints and bones separated from their places, and alleviate the overriding pain, and the fracture of the bone, and the breaking:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and the marrow in a bronze vessel and cooked oil, and put on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly easing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earthworm leaves, and boil them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for restoring the break of the bone and for calming the swelling of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violets, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of oats, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and pound, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are swollen, mix it with water of moist coriander or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of plaster stronger than the first, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of violet, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and sage, and flowers of violets and of chamomile, of all one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and pound, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken member for restoration of force unless made of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and says it should be between two, not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems reasonable to apply to the broken limb, for restoration, warm and slightly hot things, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of applying a plaster that is good for an injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the mugwort and roots of decapitated plants, or feathers of birds, and viminal and equal quantities, and bruise them, and make a plaster with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then dissolve it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone of their limb affected;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not dissolve by itself in a short time.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, without rest or relief, then hasten, and dissolve it, and remove the plaster immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip it in water, and lift up the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply a dry, moistened with water or rose oil, linen cloth, and tie it on with a nut, until you are sure of the aposteme's heat;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And reduce the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain be alleviated, then begin with a subtle bandage, and a bit of plaster, and do not strain it as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and dress it subtly until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the aposteme is hot and red and painful and swollen, all of these have been alleviated from everything, and you have need of plaster and linen, then begin again, just as you did previously.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb of what we have said, do not force the dislocation for three or four or five or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture becomes solid and the adjustment of the flesh closes in;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and bind its vein, as I have said previously;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply then a warm and cold application, every time you treat it, and let it be done each third day, and loosen the bandage a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then cut off the nourishment to the limb, and hasten what foolish doctors do, which twist the limb improperly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is malicious, and such are the works of the fearful, and I do not see anything other than giving pain and doing the work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures exist, and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the collarbone breaks the bone adjacent to the shoulder which is dislocated from the bone, as if it were crushed or beaten;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason is called this kind of fracture a "crushing".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone from both sides with a blow, and this kind of fracture is called "absolue";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is the wound of these two fractures, either great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has a dull blow, or a split, or a blow to the hip, or a fall on the hip, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing wound that approaches just to the membrane which is beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is thrown back into the bone as subtle as a goat's hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter in, and the limbs are twisted as the blacksmiths do when they strike on the anvils;
si entre li piere dedens.	if it enters between the teeth.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have a head with moist bones, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are separated as from the knees;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the extraction from them, and the inquiry with tongs, and by the decayed flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is known by that which when one discovers the bone, and one rubs upon it, if the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, beware of accidents that harm the patient, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and stretching, and palpitations, and sharp fever, and the eyes bulging out and becoming red, and other similar things in various conditions, one cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navicular bone comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to uncover the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the decayed part of the bone is corrupted, and comes the accident that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the afflicted patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if a flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a carbuncle, use what aid is necessary, and it is that you fill the hole with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the carbuncles are cooled, and be assured of the flow of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then it begins within the bone to twist, and it is done according to two manners of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is that you cut at the narrow tail end in front, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then one beats out the other cutting which is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of cuttings which are different, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of hardened iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, it is necessary that you pierce through it within, in such a way that you administer cuttings with caution, nor too deeply that they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the head, and should have at the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many, so that each one comes into his own place of the spine, so that you have supports throughout all the head;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of supports:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one support on the bone, and turn to your fingers as much as you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the support in another place a little afterwards, and thus do all around, then cut with incisions the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and extracted, it is necessary that you reset the fragment that remains of the bone to all other similar instruments, but it is necessary that it be more refined and more subtle than the other surgical tools.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or any chips, then lightly scrape them with one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tents and dressings that we have spoken of.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another manner of surgery is that which the Gauls call, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it holds very strongly, and this is its nature.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, whether it be broken or bruised, so that when you have discovered that part, then put at the head of this surgical tool, a lancet, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and the affected part is in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then make a small hammer blow above, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and be careful with the mesh that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it adheres to the bone, gently scratch the bone, for one scratches well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate just to the mesh, and the bone is cut just above, and it has small pieces, then it is necessary to render that asperity, and to remove the scales with the subtle rasp that you must have in various quantities, to apply to each place the most convenient, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with coarse rasps, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you make adjustments according to their requirement;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and it is a thing that is not denied to one who has placed his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is deep, then it is necessary that you apply a dressing of linen, according to the size of the wound, and anoint it with rose oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another doubled dressing in two or three layers, and anoint it with wine and rose oil, and put it on the first dressing;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not hurt the wound, then apply another linen on top, and do not constrict it more than necessary to hold the wound in place;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for one or two days, until the aposteme, that is to say the abscess, is appeased, then undo it, and apply medicines such as roots of lily, and powder of vetches, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer at once medicines without mordification;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and beware that the wound becomes immediately clean, so you do not leave in it any foreign object, nor allow it to gather pus, for when pus gathers on the fabric of the brain, it corrodes and festers, and brings great evil to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on the wound a caustic thing, it becomes worse by above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, that no evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no fever comes from the medicine that one has put on, which has virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue a drag, and put it on the wound;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then for the treatment of manners of treatments that are suitable, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	It is known that sometimes both parts of the knee are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this cartilage is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes inflamed or twisted, and then becomes diseased.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you apply your small bandage or plaster of the knee, and put equal to this fracture inside your bandage, and in the pouch by deficiency, until the knee regains its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the knee, and the joint cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it even at the head of a stick, a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, make one part similar to the other, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess of the swollen tumor is alleviated, then bind to the head of the knee with tendons and bandages of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind one to the other part, where the fracture is;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the openings of the knees.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say to some restorer that one must moisten the tendons in butter, and move each joint.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that it is good, but rather that they should be moistened with a confection of egg whites and powder of mallow;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then let the tendon alone, until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes the swelling bursts out of the abscess, and if the bandage is too tight inside, and it holds the break, and the patient breathes with difficulty;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do that which you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working, then put cotton moistened with rose oil, or in a little hyssop.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster made from flour of cypress, and powder of incense, mixed with water, then put on light poultices, and do not bind the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break of the nose is small, and it is broken into little pieces, then extract the suitable fragments from that, then sew the gash, and treat things that cause pain, swelling, and inflammation, as with plasters and ointments suitable to that;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has no thickness of a new wound, thus the treatment of tendons, and put bandages of plaster, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured, and there is no open wound, and the breakage is only slight, and it is not broken in two, but rather cracked within, then one must examine it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breakage is on the left jawbone, then put your right index finger, and gently push the breakage inward, and hold the other side with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone is separated into two parts, then it is necessary that you administer extension to the two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movements of the teeth are disturbed, or a rupture occurs, then hold them back with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the bruised jaw a kerchief, and put on the double cloak.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the cloak a large and well-made star or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it around the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the alignment is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then reset to its proper place what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on it, made from the powder of a mill with an abundance of egg white or flour of plant, after you have applied the kerchief;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a light plaster, and if the plasters stick, and the condition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if it has a fracture and wound together, reset the naked piece of bone in its place;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the bone as extractions provoke convulsions to that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with a flame according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have cut all these pieces of bone, and none remain, then sew the wound, if it is large, and put on it some plasters suitable to that, to draw out the pus, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture breaks several times beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	When it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are fragments, and it is more difficult to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when the break is without wound, you should have two attendants, so that one holds the injured area where the force of the break is;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the break in its place with your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor crookedness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have the need to stretch further, then put between the shoulder and the patient a round sphere of cloth, or of wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the force, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you put the break in its place, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of the ditch, because it comes from deep within, then it is necessary that the patient put his hand under his armpit, and place the middle of the shoulder on the elbow, and push the lower end of the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then take the breakage with your fingers, and if you pull it true to its debris, then it is necessary that you split on;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, then cut it with one of the incisions that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, to guard the spleen:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it seems a spoon, and is not too heavy, and should be as large as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the wound;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two parts, as you see, and one is larger, and the other is narrower, just like the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the shape is small, or you doubt it's a hot abscess, fill the wound with dressings and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, then moisten the dressing with oil, rose water and vinegar, and apply.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you apply to the bone a plaster made from powdered millstone and egg white, and apply light bandages, and put a sponge soaked in vinegar under the bandage, if you have the skill;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of a palm's width, then put a double cloth on the swelling, and apply the plaster.
