puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin stick of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and undo the healthy shoulder, and undo the diseased shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture firmly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then rewind it every day, and when the ligaments relax, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put when he sleeps a small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the joint upwards.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the fracture of the collarbone is reduced by the reduction of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and not untie it unless a bad accident happens, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then put on the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and hold it in place and let it be, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is most often restored in twenty-eight days, and in less than eight weeks.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates when it is not in its middle, and it does not get better unless by touching;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the bandage conforms to the shape of the fracture, and you rearrange it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the limb powder of millstone with a little water, and light dressings, and put over it a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a broad and subtle plaster, a little broader than the shoulder, and if the plaster is displaced from any part of the shoulder, fill in that place with cotton pads or linen strips, so that the plaster adheres evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all with a large bandage firmly, so that the plaster does not move from its place, and examine the patient each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it becomes loose, bind it, and put the plaster back in its place, and let the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is accomplished, then unbind it, and be careful, for it is not the bone that moves lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone projects forward, and presses against the heart, then make an incision, and extract it, and do what we have said concerning the treatment of abscesses with hot applications.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the toe.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the toe, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and coughing, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the bowels in the broken bone, and loses his sense completely.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient puts his back on the ground, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and joins the sides of the two ribs with his hands, and subtly makes an effort to put everything in its proper place, as much as you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and bandages made with a subtle paste of salt, or other light plaster, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the linen round to the back, and hold it tight, and look at the book every hour, and if it becomes dislocated, then hold it steady;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to loosen, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and loosen it, and rub the plaster, and address what has come from various methods of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the plaster, and hold it steady until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	It is known that the fracture of the ribs does not come from a large blow to the back, and to the inner head, and does not occur except by reason that they are fragile;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and let the pain be well for two days.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you put even the fracture, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and extract a splinter, if you are skilled in this profession.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breakage of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as from a pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it reaches to the points, and all and vomits great quantities of blood, and it is a grievous wound, and the old men have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is one of those who say that it is necessary to administer foods which inflate the stomach, in order to expel the breakage downward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, that hot abscesses do not come, if it is not come from bad blood.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then bleed it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one puts cupping glasses on the body, to suck out the humor, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	In every way, doubt exists that the veins do not attract the excesses of the body due to the lack of strength.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the body with a warm woolen cloth soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to equalize the flow of liquid around, then be cured by the treatment of pleurisy, of diet and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the bone that breaks the fabric, and doubt exists for the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the body of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put instruments in place to protect the lung;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and gently draw it back, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a postulated tumor comes, then put on it a moistened cloth with oil or rosewater, and put it on the affected area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat meanwhile the area of what is necessary for the tumor, and let the dressing be put on the affected place where it should be, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and it happens that it breaks;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, then take warning if you see their hands made soft and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when one presses and touches, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the disease will be cured, if one applies a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take care to see if the feet are weak, and if the intestines are those that are in the hands, and on the back there is swelling and vomiting without desire.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has it above their stomach, then there is vomiting without desire.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is swollen above his back and he wants to sit, then he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that they are mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	then do not labor in their cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, then the thing is more gentle.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you apply if it has a hot abscess, put on the spine oil of rose or oil of muffled wool, as long as it is appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the soothing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where they feel the pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone dislocates, then it is necessary to put a strap around the chest;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and reduce the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with an ointment of gum, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the elbow", you will put your fist into the palm of your left hand, and place it even with the other hand at your shoulder, then apply the plaster and the stake above, if you have a profession;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then hold it straight, and if there is a bone out of place, put it back, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens that the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if it happens, it does not happen with a little manipulation at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it becomes too long, and declines to the part below, and comes to the patient pain in the leg, and a sharp point, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you put your hand on top, as long as you are above the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and feel what the breakage and its shape are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the breakage is at the head solely, then put equal to that breakage, as long as it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is from the length, or it declines inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that break is apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, put on a plaster, then put on a splint of wood or of leather, and hold the break, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and anoint the limb below the ribs, until the ligament is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient that they should sleep on their sound side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a warm abscess comes, do not touch it, until the warm abscess is appeased, and put on what we have previously mentioned;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it requires, if there is no other bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and it is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulders are that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, thus one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a wooden stick of moderate thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two sticks to the two sides, and bind them high up, and sit the patient on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then put the stick with the broken arm on the stick, until it comes to the armpit, and have in the middle a curve of stick, then tie on some heavy thing where the minister's hand stretches downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the minister's hands together equal to the break, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his shoulder, and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs the servants that one of them touches what is on the fracture with his hands, and the others touch below everything to the ligament, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then hold the ligament below the fracture, and on the fracture, and stretch each of the servants to his own part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put one ligament below the armpit, and the other towards the hollow, below the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the hollow, then it is necessary to put the ligament lightly, without strain, until the fracture is even on the limb, and on the hollow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put even the fracture, if it is necessary, and hold back, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do come, do not hold back until seven days, and put on a moist plaster with oil of rose, until the abscess is appeased;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then hold back, and the manner of holding back is that you put a plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm with the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the back;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put on a bandage, and hold to the shoulder, and to the arm, so that the arm is in place of balance, if nothing deflects it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers' width, and let each splint be so large that it goes around the fracture three fingers from each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then strain on the stiles, thus as I have said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, stronger and less in aligning.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the alignment of the stiles, and the straining, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken limb, and you suspect the hot abscess, leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine each for three days the ligament, that neither swelling nor inflammation comes to the limb, or the nourishments cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it adheres, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, then do not force the dislocation further after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a cushion under the shoulder joint evenly, and watch each hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken member does not move, nor the tendons become soft;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is treated with the virtue of medicine, and the food is given which we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food should be at first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it starts to take hold, then it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be taken in 40 days of the whole;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must dislocate and administer baths and medicines to the joints for the body to be treated.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the fracture is ugly and swollen, then it stays dislocated 40 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breakage of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the " radius" and the "ulna", one of which is small, and it is the one that connects to the forearm;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is outward, towards the little elbow;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance breaking the large radius alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small radius bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, then the healing is difficult, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small radius bone alone that is broken, then it is necessary to stretch it gently, and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large radius bone, then it is necessary to pull it more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it onto the cushion, and stretch the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and let the little fingers be lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross themselves on their own body, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the patient suffers no labor;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's arms to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and one of the other ministers to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mire equal, according to its natural form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is none displaced that touches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a poultice on the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if it breaks with a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	If you take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, apply a plaster made from oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the plaster subtly on top, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and put on a plaster made from powdered millet with some egg, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger, and a little larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six splints or arms in several positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	let the fracture be in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold more firmly on the fracture than other parts, and less tightly when approaching, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the scar tissues that are on the bruised area be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, from which it is strained, be of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And bind the member and the vein after a few hours.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you rub the member with warm water, until that itching is appeased;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not be restrained from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the tightening, and if the veins are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, apply a remedy.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the nourishments cannot come to the member, because it is too constricted, then it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few hours, until the nourishment runs, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not untie them for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or put it thus: then he puts his hands at his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and of degeneration, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have said before, there are few fractures, and it does not come more than a flow of blood many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or pierced, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then he puts his hand on the extended toe, and extends the mangled bones, and puts the nerves in their place, as long as they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies a plaster and a poultice, if an abscess does not come, then he puts in a probe according to the quantity of the humor;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be enveloped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is on the inner side of the belly of the foot, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the probe be of wood as soft as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the fingers, it is necessary that you put a probe on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is closed and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the cloth between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if a fracture comes to one of the two bones, it is the pulse, set it even, as it is necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and strain with the sole of the foot, and if you see that a small straight stick is put in place to lift the fracture, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in one of the other bones, such as in the elbow or one of the others, set it even, and bind it with the healthy bone that is nearby;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them together in a bandage, which is of use, or you put on a stick, like a poultice;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the treatment of hot abscesses, and heal what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often fractured, and one can see it well when it turns to the front and back;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is thus on one side of the fracture, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient puts his hands on his face, then each assistant extends his hand to his side equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then let one of the assistants be at the groin, and the other assistant below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the assistant be at the knee, and let the extension be below;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the doctor's bones evenly by his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, so that abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it cool down, then return to your work and to its treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The ligature is made in a similar way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a bandage doubled two or three times, and in addition the superfluous, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the hip, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread come out above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn around the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put on the fracture these, and put a steel rod against the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make equal pressure, then begin to tie firmly two or three turns around the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you go up from the fracture, the less it is tightened;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then understand the two heads of the thread that you have passed between the thigh and the hip, and in place III these which are dislocated, then return to the dislocation at the head of the thread, until you come down to the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it steady, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess nor swelling nor any similar thing comes to it.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then loosen it, and treat what comes from it, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if it has pieces of bone that are pricked, then reset them in their place, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then reset by cutting the place, and pulling strongly;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip is broken thus when one puts these, as in the shoulder or the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	In every way, during the restoration, do not conceal from the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And be aware that the hip is restored in the joint, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the complications.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the cavity of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Be aware that in the hollow of the knee there is little breaking, but it often swells.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no more than a fissure, or a perforation, and has a wound, and without a wound, and that feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when one puts back what is broken in its place, as long as it is assembled with what can be put together;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put on a round splint, if you are skilled in it, and hold it as is necessary, then consider all the treatments that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses, heat, and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Put to each accident what is suitable for it, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Be aware that in the leg there are II bones, one of which is called by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it has the same kind of fracture as the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg becomes crooked on every side.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it becomes deformed at the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it affects the foot;
et torne desoz.	and becomes misshapen.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then we apply extension, and put it in place, and lay the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but however, it is necessary to break it if the wound is bad, and it has many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and adjust according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of cloth that press the thigh on one side and the other, and are as long as the thigh from the knee to the hip;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap two layers one over the other above and below, and tie it in the middle, and with this binding the thigh will not decline to the right or left, and thus it is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and let no one administer a bandage as long as the thigh, made of cloth, and put it on the thigh to prevent movement, and properly apply it in the fracture or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or some other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you treat him until he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle comes no fracture, but to the bones of the foot come sometimes fractures and to the two knees, and it does not happen that they are broken in many different ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then have the patient put their foot on the ground, as if they were going to fly, and then put your foot on top of theirs, where the bones are raised, then press down until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put a plaster and bandages on, and put two small towels under the belly of the foot, then hold the foot firmly in place, then that you have wrapped the dressings around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the linen bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are some of the fingers broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then put beneath the foot that table that I spoke of, and hold it firmly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and hold the table firmly beneath the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be standing on the top of the table away from the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone in the nature of the woman is fractured, if it is made to swell, then it is inclined to the back part, and held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the bowl with the nature of the patient's poultice, and in it put as much as my fist;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then undress the woman, and lift the back a little by little, and then press the poultice, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the fist;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the poultice, and when she has urinated, put it back on, and do this for seven days or within;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If it will restore the fracture, and you see, take a bladder of barley, and tie a thread to the perforation, and put all the bladder in the nostril.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the thread strongly, until the bladder is inflated from within:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the nostril will return the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and let it be like that for some hours, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone that gives the shoulder its shape in a man or woman is fractured, restore it in this way as we have said for the bone of the thigh;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who puts their study and effort into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in several dispositions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	Hear the wounds.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	On the rod, when it is broken, take a handful of ivy and bind the rod;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap tape around, and let it be for three days or four days, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of a fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the healings that we have spoken of bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then anoint with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then recommence to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if apostems or abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if apostems or abscesses do come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the apostems are appeased, and do not touch it on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would cause a bad accident to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the heart without covering, then you must put it in place lightly with your hands, for a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not prepared to put it in your hands, then reset it with this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the master to take 3 or 4, according to what he needs for each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved head is placed on the top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and strike it once, as long as it regrows, and let one be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the bandages cannot hold the bone well, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, so that the bandage has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an instrument suitable for that, either an incision or a saw, to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone of splinters and small shards.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not yet in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Make so that it stays in its place, then moisten the dressing with black styptic wine, and properly if it is in a splint.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound cerote or anything else where it has oil, so that it does not cause suppuration and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the dressing;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused death or corruption to come upon the patient;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the dressing be softer and more gentle than other dressings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that an evil accident will occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the body, then it is not necessary to apply these;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, on the body of the dressings, a piece of cloth, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days a swelling around the wound, remove what you had applied on top of everything, and put on a healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is swollen and sore.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the swelling falls away gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but instead discharges pus, with small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you touch the wound with a probe, and remove all those loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears on the limb, or another kind of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in its chapter previously.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and it opens onto the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or of the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not treat it immediately, because many times death comes, but let it be until it purifies;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it will close after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruises that come upon the abscess
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times they come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance it cannot make the limbs perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then that the nose is not cold:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acaice, and other similar things, then that you prepare one of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with a bath of warm water or with vinegar;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on a nut in a pestle, and constrain it well, and do not dislodge it with the hand for a long time;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislodge it, and start again another one, until the swelling of the knot is reduced;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you constrain on a well-made piece of splint;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of splints is that they reduce all the swellings above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling is already converted into hardness like stone, and it needs to be cut, then they cut above it, and make the excess flesh apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you raise it with a razor, until it is reduced, and the treatment until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and it remains after the member is weak and subtle, then it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	Because one of them is for this reason tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it had too many ties, and the nourishments could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of a multitude of irritations;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, not in their proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you should make the patient eat, and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in it;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer a bath, and give joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply poultice to the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the irritation of the skin is often soothed, until the nourishment flows to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb twists after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limbs are twisted after the restoration, and the broken bones are exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not retain its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if you do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these practices are blamed, and great evils come from them, and death often results;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the nodules and the hardness are recent, then it is necessary that they be treated with warm water, or that softening herbs be applied, such as leaves of violets, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diacalons, and take the muscle of violet, and mix it with fat of goose or oil of cypress, and apply the plaster;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	You take fat figs, and you crush them with a little fenugreek, and similar medicines that ease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the node is soothed by continuously and lengthily rubbing it with a moist hand.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the movement be eased on the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuosity is inflamed and hardened, like stone, and needs to be worked with iron, then it must be bored into just to the bone, and subtly and lightly incised;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put caution and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begin the books of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is necessary now to bring back into alignment.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one is late, the limbs become inflamed, and by chance, if it resets by itself to the limb;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not suitable to move it to the hole where it is inflamed:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in any case, when this happens, if you make the patient sane, then leave him, until the abscesses or ulcers are appeased;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member from the cold and oily water, then reset it gently, and treat each member as its cure will come into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated and loose, and the dislocation of both is in two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are a little loosened from their places, and made a little soft;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	where they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the pis, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and envelops the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through many different positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and complete, then it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the minister guides the head of the patient, and puts his fingers in the pouch of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on the lower part;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers of the hands are held apart, in order to set it straight;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And look at the step that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reset is difficult, likewise if it is the two jaws together, apply warm water and oil, until they are reset lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	nor do we speak of resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then put on dressings moistened with a mixture made of oil, honey, and wax, and bind them lightly with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be placed between two pillows, so that they do not move either to the right or to the left, nor exert themselves to chew, but take light food, until the pains are diminished, and the jaws are numb;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then chew what he wants lightly, and do not exert himself to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their proper position, then come fever and accustomed sweats, and by chance a discharge of stomach, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a prediction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he whom it has befallen dies in eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fracture
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fracture cannot dissolve the bone within the continuity of the body and the fat, and is dissolved sometimes in the intestine, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient puts his arm under his back, and stretches out his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the shoulder forcefully with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and bind it tight, and hold in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the part that is turned towards the hip cannot become dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it becomes dislocated again, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and bind it tight, and hold in place, and instruct the patient to rest as long as he is healthy;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is when it becomes dislocated at the lower part of the joint;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second one is at the part of the foot;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates at the upper part, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind the shoulder, and does not dislocate within for the kidneys;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially to those who have little flesh, for to these the joint slips out quickly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	to those who have enough flesh, it slips with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance there is to some men a blow or fracture, and the shoulder is swollen from a hot abscess, and it is thought that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you test it, until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that the dislocation when it is downwards towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the bone touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an elbow;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his shoulders, nor move with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is recent, or if the patient himself is not malformed.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers lift the patient's hand up high, then put their fingers below the bone, and lift the joint forcefully up to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister lifts the hand and stretches it upwards, then puts it back in place;
si venra hastanment.	if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in lesser hours afterwards, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and let the enema be made softening and soothing, such as a decoction of liquorice and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be administered;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient be rubbed on their back, and put under the armpit a piece of linen cloth equal, not too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the piece of cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another attendant holds the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder returns now to its proper place, and you will see if it is reset in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you make someone who is bigger than the patient be present at home;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and let it be straight towards the side of the sick person, and put the shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another assistant pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then hang with him something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And one resets it in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that you stick a stick into the ground, of which the head is as thick as the wrist, and is neither too big nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then let it be placed under the patient, but so that he has his shoulders draped up, and the patient is standing from the length of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand should be extended downwards from the other side of the shoulder, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take the size of 4 fingers in width and 3 fingers in length, which has its head bent to enter into the hollow of the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie around the head of the fist a soft cloth, so that the fist does not harm the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm on the fist of the long one, and tie the shoulder to the fist, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on a stick of a chair of the width, and let the hands be extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint returns to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, then you must put under the shoulder a layer of wool equal, then put the plaster prepared with powder of millstone, and incense and egg white, on the entire shoulder and around, then strain under the shoulder firmly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and hold the hand to his neck, and let the other hand remain in place.
